1936.04.27

With Yongjian as the Center: Opening of the Japanese Military Officers' Conference; Military Officers from Various Parts of North China Participate; Discussion Focuses on Anti-Communism; Continuing Discussions Planned for This Morning; Final Decision on Future Implementation Plans; Ishii Will Take the Conference Results to Changchun Today for Discussions 1

(Tianjin) The North China Japanese Military Officers' Conference was held at the Zhang Garden Commander's Residence at 3 PM on the 26th. With Yongjian as the center, over twenty people attended, including military officers, staff officers, and attached unit leaders from various regions. First, Yongjian reported on his attendance at the division commander's conference after returning to Japan and announced the opinions of the army headquarters. Subsequently, military officers from various regions reported on the current situation of their missions and the current anti-communist diplomatic situation. Finally, discussions were held according to the scope of the regulations regarding: Opinions on anti-communism in North China; Steps for economic development; General diplomatic surveillance attitude in Hebei and Chahar; Attention to general public security within Hebei and Chahar; and Promotion of transportation in Hebei and Chahar. The meeting adjourned at 8 PM. The military officers plan to leave Tianjin separately on the 27th to return to their posts. Senior Staff Officer Ishii will take the conference results to Changchun on the morning of the 27th for discussions and then return to Japan to report. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) The participants in the military officers' conference on the 26th were Yongjian, Matsumuro, Hamada, Ishii, Nakai, Do, Kyou, attached officer Hayashi, and Okada, among others, as well as eight key members of the Tianjin Garrison Army. Additionally, seven military officers from Yulin, Zhangjiakou, and Suisui, and Ji'nan, including Hosoki, Omoto, Wachi, Hayama, Ishino, Ueno, and Hesaki, attended. Those present were Infantry Captain Mutaguchi, Tianjin Captain Kayashima, Tanggu Captain Kagawa, Tangshan Captain Hinobe, Tianjin Naval Officer Kubota, and Qinhuangdao Naval Officer Kuwahara, totaling six people. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) At 9 AM on the 26th, Yongjian convened a conference of Japanese military officers from Tianjin, Beiping, Zhangjiakou, Suiyuan, Taiyuan, and Shanhaiguan at Zhang Garden. He first reported on the situation of attending the division commander's conference and conveyed the intentions of the Japanese military headquarters. The meeting continued in the afternoon, with each military officer reporting on the situation in their respective locations. Finally, decisions were made regarding future work plans. The meeting adjourned late in the evening. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) Senior Staff Officer Ishii of the Tianjin Japanese Garrison Army is scheduled to return to Japan via Northeast China by plane on the morning of the 27th to represent Yongjian at the Chief of Staff meeting. He is expected to return to Tianjin in two weeks. Additionally, Takeshita went to Changchun from Tianjin on the 26th to take up his new position as the head of the 3rd Section of the Kwantung Army. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) Colonel Nagatsu, the head of the China Section of the Japanese Army General Staff Headquarters, the new successor to Kita, came to Tianjin on the morning of the 26th to meet with Tada and Yongjian to convey the intentions of the Army Central Department. He is scheduled to go to Beiping on the 27th and then go to Sui County for inspection before returning to Japan. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) Because a portion of the cases at the Japanese military officers' conference has not been fully discussed, it will continue to be held on the morning of the 27th. With the exception of Imai, Mutaguchi, Tsunekawa, and others who had already returned to Beiping on the 26th, the remaining officers will also leave Tianjin separately after the meeting on the 27th. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Xiao Zhenying Returns to Tianjin: Continuing Negotiations on Hebei and Chahar 2

(Beiping) Xiao Zhenying returned to Tianjin this morning. After attending the Economic Committee meeting, I returned to Tianjin to report to Song. If there are important cases in the Economic Committee next week, I will come to Beiping again. Due to the sincerity between China and Japan in Hebei-Chahar diplomacy, the future is expected to proceed smoothly. I will continue negotiations after returning to Tianjin. Separately, the Chinese and Japanese officials responsible for Hebei-Chahar diplomacy will begin negotiations in Tianjin in early May, and a solution will be sought for general issues in these negotiations. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) Xiao Zhenying returned to Tianjin and plans to meet with Matsumuro and Yongjian on the morning of the 27th with Chen Juesheng to continue discussions on Hebei-Chahar anti-communist diplomacy. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Beiping) Recently, Hebei-Chahar diplomacy has focused on the anti-communism issue and is being discussed in Tianjin. If this issue is resolved, the Hebei and eastern Chahar issues can be resolved without further complications. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) The cases of Korean occupation of housing and suppression of drugs are being negotiated by the authorities, but the Japanese side has only agreed to assist, and there are no concrete measures yet. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Kawagoe's Scheduled Return to Japan 3

(Tianjin) Kawagoe has decided to leave Tianjin on the 3rd, spend a night in Tanggu, and return to Japan on the Changjiang Maru on the 4th. The official ceremony for his appointment as the Ambassador to China will be held on the 10th, and he will come to China to present his credentials in the capital at the end of next month. The handover of the Tianjin Consulate has been completed. At 7 PM on the 26th, he will attend a farewell banquet hosted by key members of the Mitsui, Mitsubishi, and Residents' Association. He will visit various parties on the 1st to bid farewell. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) The Association of Japanese Students in Tianjin, initiated by Chen Juesheng, has scheduled a farewell banquet for Kawagoe at the West Lake Hotel on the afternoon of the 1st. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Strange Ships Discovered Cruising in Fujian Waters 4

(Xiamen) According to sources in Quanzhou, an unidentified warship of unknown nationality without a flag was discovered cruising in the waters between Huian and Chongwu on the 24th. Two unmarked aircraft took off from the ship and soared over the coast. The Second District Public Office was informed and dispatched a boat to investigate, but the ship had disappeared without a trace. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Meets with Military and Political Leaders in Guizhou; Qian Dajun Talks About the Impending Elimination of Xiao and He's Bandits; Liu Jianshu Flies from Chongqing to Pay His Respects 5

(Guiyang) Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, accompanied by Qian Dajun and others, flew from Yunnan to Guiyang on the 25th by Boeing aircraft. Those who welcomed him at the Qingzhen Airport included Liu Xing, Cao Jingyuan, Guo Siyan, Hao Mengling, and members of the provincial party headquarters, the heads of various departments of the provincial government, and several hundred division and brigade commanders. Tens of thousands of staff members from various agencies, civil organizations, and schools lined up along the road from Guiyang City to Touqiao to await his arrival. At precisely noon, the Boeing landed at the airport, and military music played loudly. All welcomers stood at attention and saluted. Chiang got off the plane, looking energetic and healthy, and nodded with a smile in response. He then entered Guiyang with Liu and rested at the commander's headquarters after taking a car. He met with various senior officials. Qian Dajun told reporters from the Central News Agency that his impression of Yunnan was excellent and that the officials and people of the province were particularly respectful and obedient to the leader with great enthusiasm. The remnants of the Xiao and He bandits have now fled to Heqing. Our Guo, Fan, and Li columns are still following them. The terrain there is complex, but the elimination of the remnants is imminent. Also, Liu Jianshu arrived in Qingzhen by plane from Chongqing at 1:30 PM on the 25th and immediately took a car into the city to pay respects to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. He will go to Yunnan to supervise the suppression of bandits soon. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 25th)

(Guiyang) Chairman Chiang Kai-shek met with various military leaders on the morning of the 26th and with various members of the provincial government in the afternoon. He inquired about military and political affairs in the province. Qian Dajun and others inspected the New Life Movement Promotion Association at 1 PM on the 26th. The director of the association, Guo Siyan, led them to visit and watch the Miao people dancing. Qian and others greatly praised the association's work. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Remaining Bandits in Shanxi Still Attempting to Struggle; Our Army Decides to Adopt a Strategy of Encirclement; Pillboxes Along the Bandit Areas Are Being Actively Constructed; Large Numbers of Captured Bandits Released with Musical Accompaniment; Yang Hucheng Establishes Headquarters in Hancheng 6

(Taiyuan) In Qixian, Wucheng, Zhen, Beizhuang, Sujiazhuang, and other places, Guan's troops defeated the bandit army and seized dozens of mortars and machine guns, and over two hundred rifles. Over three hundred formal Red Army soldiers were captured. These captured goods have all been sent to the province. In addition to the previous award of 5,000 yuan to the division, an additional 8,000 yuan has now been awarded. Over a thousand Red Army soldiers have been captured by our forces on all routes and have been sent to the rear for rehabilitation, or provided with funds to return to their hometowns. Ninety-eight people, including Deng Changqing, the company commander of Peng Dehuai's bandit guard battalion, who were captured, recently expressed their complete awakening due to our preferential treatment and jointly published a letter of respect to the Red Army comrades, which was distributed to the bandit side to promote their awakening. Currently, Mao Zedong personally commands the remaining bandit troops. Our side has decided to adopt a strategy of encirclement, and pillboxes are being actively constructed along the bandit areas. Mao Xuzai, the Yulin Administrative Inspector Commissioner, came to Bing yesterday to meet Yan and Chen to report on the recent situation in northern Shaanxi. According to him, Liu Zidan has indeed been injured and is receiving medical treatment at Yongnian Fort in northern Shaanxi. The bandit forces in that area have been greatly reduced. Only a few remnants, including Wang Zhaoxiang, Liu Zidan, and his brother Jinfan, are left east of Yulin, each with no more than a few hundred people. Du Dichang, the false chief of staff of Zidan, was killed by Gao Guizi's troops, and the majority was disintegrated. Mao left Bing for Beijing this afternoon to attend the National Administrative Conference, accompanied by Kang Wang and his entourage, who returned to Suiyuan via Datong this morning. Kong Lingxun, the division commander of the Central Army, came to Bing last night to pay his respects. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Taiyuan) The entire 4th Division of the pseudo-First Army Corps was intercepted by Guan Qizhen's troops. After two hours of fierce fighting, the bandits were unable to hold on and retreated. Guan's division joined Yang Chengyuan's troops to pursue. Guan believes that in this operation, the bandit army refused to surrender unless they were absolutely desperate, entirely because the bandit leaders used the slogan that the National Army killed prisoners to scare them. Therefore, the division captured 274 bandits and, with the approval of Chen Cheng, conducted separate training, provided them with food and drink, and gave each person ten yuan for travel expenses. They were escorted out of the city with a military band and released. The other captured pseudo-guerrilla teams were also released. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Xi'an) In order to facilitate the command of the suppression of the remaining bandits, Yang Hucheng has specially established headquarters in Hancheng to command the Feng and Sun armies, quickly advancing towards northern Shaanxi, and blocking various crossings along the river, and establishing contact with friendly forces on both banks to prevent the bandits from fleeing west. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Ning Shiyi Returns to Nanjing

(Nanjing) After the Red Bandits in northern Shaanxi crossed the river and invaded Jin City, they were eventually defeated by friendly forces between Zhongyang and Shilou. Some of our soldiers were also injured and transported back to Taiyuan for treatment. Chairman Chiang specially sent Ning Shiyi, a major general section chief of the military, to Bing at the beginning of the month with a large number of goods to represent his condolences to all the soldiers and to inspect the front lines and convey his words of encouragement. Ning completed his mission in Shanxi and arrived in Nanjing on the afternoon of the 26th and is scheduled to report to Minister He in the morning of the 27th. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

剿匪 on the Borders of Shaanxi

(Xi'an) Our army recently pursued and suppressed the Red Bandits. According to reports: On the Shaanxi-North Shaanxi front, the bandit remnants in western Shanxi gathered west of Yonghe, Qingshui Pass, and Madou Pass, attempting to return to Shaanxi to cause trouble. Our Sun and Wang columns advanced north from Yichuan and Fushi on the 22nd. In the Shaanxi-Gansu border area, the remnants of Huang Ziven's bandits were defeated by our army. On the 19th, they led approximately six or seven hundred remnants of infantry and cavalry to Zhiluo Town in a state of extreme disarray. Our Chang column followed and suppressed them, arriving at Liuyazhen and Luomadian on the 23rd, capturing over a hundred bandits along the way and seizing fifty guns. The road they traversed was mountainous and rugged, with no traces of human habitation for over twenty years. Our army cleared the road while striving to advance. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 25th)

(Xi'an) Report on the suppression of bandits in the Shaanxi-Gansu border area: According to reports, on the 22nd, the Xiao Jingguang unit of the pseudo-28th Army, approximately two thousand strong, fled from Zhi County back to Linzhen Town, north of Ganquan, in a state of exhaustion, indicating that they had suffered heavy losses in Shanxi. Since the 21st, over two thousand people from the pseudo-26th and 29th Armies have gathered in Ganquan and Fushi, attempting to resist the National Army. The pseudo-Shaanxi-Gansu Provincial Government has moved from Taotong to Xiadaigang, northwest of Ganquan. Several hundred bandits under Huang Ziven have fled to the Zhiluo Town area in a state of utter disarray. On the southern Shaanxi front, Chen Guangrui's bandits have fled to the Zhuling Pass area, where our army is fiercely suppressing them. Wang Sanchun's forces have fled to the Dahangxi area north of Wanyuan, where our army has captured many of them. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Bandits in Eastern and Northern Fujian

(Fuzhou) After our army's strict encirclement and suppression of the bandits in various parts of eastern and northern Fujian, the main forces have suffered heavy losses and have lost the ability to invade. The Liu Ying bandits who scattered from Zhejiang, after being suppressed by one of our divisions, fled south to Dong Jiyang in Shouning, where they were intercepted by the Third Security Regiment. The bandits fled towards Xianfeng. On the 24th, a unit of the regiment actively advanced to search and suppress them. In this battle, one bandit leader and fourteen bandit soldiers were killed, two were captured, and three guns were seized. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

(Fuzhou) The Liu Ying bandits who fled to Xianfeng in Shouning were defeated by the Yi Qiji Regiment on the 25th, killing dozens of pseudo-officers and soldiers. Liu Ying barely escaped with his life. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Results of Smuggling in North China: Decline in the Import of Legitimate Japanese Goods into Tianjin: A Twofold Decrease from March 1st to April 15th Compared to the Same Period Last Year 7

(Tianjin) From March 1st to April 15th, due to rampant smuggling, the legitimate import of Japanese goods into Tianjin decreased twofold compared to the same period last year. The total amount of goods shipped from Dalian to Tianjin was 5,305 tons, from Korea to Tianjin was 48 tons, and from Japan to Tianjin was 20,892 tons. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) Recently, smugglers have increasingly used civilian boats on the southern Grand Canal and the Ziya River to transport goods to the interior for cut-price sales, hoping to clear out stockpiled goods in Tianjin. The Hebei-Chahar authorities have instructed the Wuhu River Maritime Public Security Bureau to assist customs and railways in strictly cracking down on smuggling. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

A Certain Party Purchases and Transports Reed Salt in Eastern Hebei for Export and Sells It at Low Prices in Coastal Towns 8

(Tianjin) A certain party purchases and transports reed salt in eastern Hebei for export and sells it at low prices in coastal towns, disrupting the salt business. The authorities have urged the Reed Salt Export General Office to be established quickly and to adopt a commercial management system. The Longlu Salt Envoy, who also serves as the General Manager, only supervises everything, while the actual responsibility lies with the commercial co-organizers. Two additional branch offices will be established to facilitate contact with purchasers and transporters. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has consolidated the salt industry, unified salt weights and prices, and gradually completed the work of raising salt taxes in order to reorganize the salt affairs. To facilitate management and reduce smuggling, it plans to build warehouses and mounds on various coasts. However, due to the enormous cost, it has specifically ordered the salt transport envoys of various coasts to prepare plans and submit them to the ministry for approval so that the situation can be weighed and implemented separately. This plan is a preparation for the implementation of the new salt law. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

In the afternoon, over ten papers were presented. The meeting adjourned at 5 PM. Ge Guangting Arrives in Jinan Yesterday to Discuss with Han About Building the Jinan-Liaocheng Road 14

According to Ge, the purpose of his visit to Jinan this time is to discuss with Chairman Han the issues of enlisting workers to build the Jinan-Liaocheng Road and raising private shares. The charter for this plan is currently being revised by the Ministry of Railways and preparations will be made as soon as it is promulgated. The road will be jointly operated by the government and commerce, with the provincial government, the Jiaoji Railway, and the Ministry of Railways each responsible for a portion of the construction funds. Private shares will be raised as much as possible, and it is planned to set up an office in Jinan in the future. The name is yet to be determined. All personnel will be transferred from the Jiaoji Railway in order to save costs. The Ministry of Railways has approved the extension of the Zhangdian-Boshan branch line. The required materials will be old materials from the Jiaoji Railway, and the labor cost is only several hundred thousand yuan. The line is relatively short, and the preparations are simple, so construction can begin soon. However, there are many mountains in Xintai and Laiwu, making construction difficult, so it can only be carried out slowly. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Factory Establishment of Breastfeeding Rooms and Daycare Centers: Outline of Measures Approved and Implemented by the Executive Yuan 15

(Nanjing) In order to seek the welfare of workers' children, factories are ordered to establish breastfeeding rooms and daycare centers. The outline of the measures has been formulated by the ministry and has been revised and approved for implementation by the Executive Yuan. The ministry is now urging its realization. The outline consists of eighteen articles, stipulating that factories that employ 100 or more married female workers on a regular basis should set up breastfeeding rooms, and those that employ less than 100 may jointly set up breastfeeding rooms with nearby factories. Also, factories that employ 300 or more married female workers should set up daycare centers in addition to breastfeeding rooms, and those that employ less than 300 may jointly set up daycare centers with nearby factories. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Tea merchants are jointly emailing the Ministry of Industry and the Economic Committee, and the two provincial governments express their support because of the low interest on loans and the elimination of exploitation. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Current Affairs Commentary

The Arab-Jewish Ethnic Conflict in Palestine 17

— Lang

The Arab-Jewish ethnic dispute in Palestine, which had been calm for many years, erupted again on the 19th due to a minor incident. The seriousness of the situation is no less than that of the 1929 "Wailing Wall" incident. According to dispatches from foreign news agencies, dozens of people have been killed or injured in clashes between Arabs and Jews. Transportation between Tel Aviv and Jaffa has been cut off. Arabs in the port of Haifa have launched a general strike. Many Jewish-owned shops have been forced to close. Demonstrations by both Arab and Jewish communities have resumed. It is difficult to predict how the situation will develop. However, based on the past history of Arab-Jewish ethnic disputes, this incident will not have a satisfactory ending in the short term.

Palestine is originally the homeland of the Jews. However, because they have been scattered around the world for a long time, the majority of the people living in Palestine are Arabs, numbering about 700,000. The Jews, on the other hand, are a minority, numbering only about 200,000. In recent years, Jews scattered around the world have suffered various abuses from governments of various countries and deeply felt the pain of not having a homeland. Therefore, they have the idea of rebuilding their homeland. The so-called Zionist organization aims to revive the Jewish homeland. During the Great War, Britain wanted to obtain the help of Jews from all over the world and promised to support the Jewish restoration movement. In November 1917, Lord Balfour, on behalf of the British government, issued a famous declaration, stating that "the British government is very willing to see the Jews build a national home in Palestine and is willing to provide various assistance to achieve this goal." After the war, Palestine was designated as a British Mandate. Therefore, the movement of Jews returning to their homeland became more rapid. Jews from all over the world organized groups, raised funds for the construction of their homeland, purchased land in Palestine, and relocated a large number of Jews back there. As a result, the power of the Jews in Palestine increased greatly, which aroused serious opposition from the local Arabs. Originally, the Arabs regarded Palestine as their place of residence. The large-scale invasion of the Jews to engage in the restoration movement was tantamount to infringing on the inherent rights of the Arabs. The two demands put forward by the Arabs in this conflict (restricting Jewish immigration and land acquisition) were aimed at this point. The Jews, on the other hand, believe that Palestine is their homeland. Now they are returning to their homeland to build a national home because they cannot bear the oppression of governments of various countries, which is very justified. Moreover, this restoration movement has been supported by Britain and the League of Nations. Although both sides have sufficient reasons, their actual interests cannot be reconciled after all. Moreover, their religions are different. Therefore, serious ethnic disputes break out from time to time. In the 1929 "Wailing Wall" incident, hundreds of people were killed or injured on both sides. Although no major disputes have occurred in recent years, recently, a serious conflict has erupted again due to a minor incident.

Britain's policy toward the Arab-Jewish ethnic conflict is ostensibly neutral and acts as a mediator. But in reality, it uses the conflict between the two communities to consolidate its rule in Palestine. We know that Palestine is a key location in the eastern Mediterranean, connecting the Suez Canal, and occupies an important position in transportation and military affairs. Britain will never give it up. To consolidate its ruling power in Palestine, the smartest way is to make full use of the conflict between the Arab and Jewish communities, so that they fight each other internally, and do not pay attention to British rule. Britain's support for the Jewish nation-building movement during the Great War and the change in its policy toward Palestine in 1930 were based on this principle. Under these circumstances, we sincerely hope that the Arab and Jewish communities can awaken, stop internal conflicts, and shift the focus of struggle. Only in this way can the oppressed Arab and Jewish communities gain complete liberation and not be subjected to imperialist fetters for a long time.

(Beiping) All foreign missionaries in Xinping, 80 miles east of Shenyang, have withdrawn due to a serious disturbance in the area. Moreover, local people guide them, so the Japanese army's expeditionary force is exhausted, suffers great blows, loses more than 100,000 lives, and spends hundreds of millions of Japanese yen. A Look at the Depression in the Forestry Industry by Li Yin-gong, Agricultural College of National Central University 53

Scholars rarely fail to attribute the decline of our national livelihood and the scarcity of products to the failure of agriculture and forestry education to follow the correct path. I dare not offer much rebuttal. I will focus on the depression in the forestry industry and offer a fair assessment, summarizing its major causes to inform the nation. The devastation of forests and woodlands in our country has reached its peak. On the one hand, the remaining forests lack accurate surveys of their volume (the Forestry Department of National Central University is undertaking this work and will publish its reports in installments). In international comparisons of resources, they are rarely included in statistics. On the other hand, the vast area of barren mountains and unproductive hills is disproportionate. Population density varies, and the need for fuel has not been universally met by replacing wood with coal. The industrial and commercial use of forest products is also in its infancy. Considering the national crisis, and even a tentative thought on national defense reserves, the direct and indirect supply that depends on forestry is limitless, yet the current situation is like this. How should we approach the plan to remedy this situation? This is a major question. In fact, there is a solution: focus on forestry administration, cultivate talent and land, be open and honest, remove obstacles, and do not sit idly by, paralyzed, to avoid committing the great sin of misleading the country. Then, there is hope. I will now describe the causes of the depression in our forestry industry in broad strokes as follows:

The Collective Application of Forestry Talent is Impossible. Our study of forestry is based on that of other countries. For more than twenty years, the number of people studying relevant subjects has been limited, as can be seen from the fact that the membership list of the Chinese Forestry Society has fewer than 150 people. Adding to this, the government has failed to employ them in accordance with their skills. Over time, many have changed careers, accounting for a significant portion. Some have failed in forestry and become discouraged. To this day, only half have persevered. Among them, disagreements are common, factions arise, and even unwillingness to cooperate and mutual undermining are inevitable. As a result, the lack of progress in national undertakings is undeniable.

The General Public Lacks Awareness of the Importance of Forestry. The Zhouli (Rites of Zhou) established officials to manage mountains and fields, a system that has not been followed for a long time. Later generations, such as Su Dongpo, planted mulberry trees to make a living, and Dai Junshan wrote "On Planting Trees," saying, "I secretly bear the ambition of the age, wanting to shelter all the people in the world, so that they do not lose their sustenance." Almost everyone regarded forestry as a long-term solution. The prevailing ethos of the late Qing Dynasty was superficial, with a focus on quick results obscuring long-term vision. Seeing that the benefits of forestry were slow to materialize, they were willing to abandon it. People in politics seem to have the mindset of "five days as magistrate of the capital," neglecting the long-term plan of "ten years to grow trees." To give an example from recent years, after traveling to Mount Huangshan, I saw that the trees there were thriving and that it was a place for the study of natural plants. I thought that a forest botanical garden should be established, imitating Mount Lu, to serve as a center for testing the products of the South China region. In addition to proposing this at the first meeting of the Huangshan Construction Committee, I repeatedly appealed to the authorities, but was never adopted. How could one not be discouraged? Such things are too numerous to mention. Furthermore, in the agricultural community, there are those who hold important positions in agricultural education or testing agencies who either downplay forestry or dismiss it as insignificant. This is also unwise. Furthermore, in provinces known as pioneers, such as Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the annual agricultural and forestry administration system is changed almost every year, either due to the inconstancy of trusting people or due to budget cuts that lead to reorganization. As a result, local undertakings are frequently destroyed. Even more so, local forestry administration does not aim at talent but rather harmonizes factions and distributes power equally. At best, its regulatory power is limited to superficial formalities and completing a task. May I ask, can the lifeline that is crucial to national prosperity and the cause of saving the nation be carried out in this way for long?

Forestry Administration Seems Nonexistent; Rare to Hear of National Operations. Our country's forestry administration began around the same time as the early Republic of China, but the promulgation of the Forest Law is still recent. The current Ministry of Industry has an estimate of the area of forests and barren mountains nationwide, which I will not discuss for now. As for state-owned forests, only central forest areas are managed, and the scope is too small. Moreover, protective forests have not been established, so it is no wonder that disasters continue. The management of provincial forests has not been unified, so it is no wonder that each province acts on its own. There has been no consultation with the Ministry of Interior to investigate land, and suitable land is not being utilized. There has been no consultation with the Ministry of Finance, so the expansion of state-owned forests, the purchase of barren mountains, and the protection and other facilities are without funds. All these are points that our country should pay attention to in the future. Even if the government does not want central control of forestry administration, it must delegate power to the localities and constantly supervise and audit their achievements from the central government, and examine and approve their plans. In short, if everything has not yet been put on the right track, then the responsibility of leadership lies with the government. Once the business becomes tense, then rely on experts to work together to assist. Given the current state of our country's mountains and wilderness, the management of forestry cannot be accomplished by the manpower and financial resources of one side alone. I have always believed that land area is limited and close to villages should be entrusted to small farmers to do their best to integrate agriculture, forestry, and animal husbandry. Vast areas away from villages should encourage local public groups to operate, and even impose barren mountain taxes to encourage them. The entry of the state may be limited to protection forests, which is lighter and easier, but it must employ the right people, so that their interactions are evident, and the expenditure of funds must be public, so as to reduce waste.

The Protection of Forests and Woodlands Lacks Effective Measures. According to advanced forestry countries in the East and West, huge sums of money are spent annually on protection administration as a matter of course. The methods of protection all start with the strict implementation of severe laws to warn the stubborn. Over time, the people develop habits and do not violate the forests in the slightest. Our country cannot do this, so most forests have been destroyed. Therefore, if we want to develop forestry in the future, the protection of political power is indispensable. Moreover, the soil layer of most of today's barren mountains is still thick and usable, especially the hills in the south and central regions, where there are many wild tree species. Here is a table of the percentage of wild trees in the school's Bufu Forest Farm:

[Missing table data]

The trees in the table represent the types of miscellaneous trees that grow naturally in Nanjing. If they are not destroyed in winter, or if villagers are restricted to only cutting grass and not damaging the cone trees, a native forest will inevitably rise up in three to five years. Those who have traveled to Mount Lu deeply feel that the forests of that mountain can be protected in this way without the need for artificial procedures. How many such places are there in various provinces? Moreover, those who carry firewood for a living in towns and cities should be subject to police inspection. If they have invaded a protected forest, they should be fined for selling and buying the same crime. Over time, this abuse can be stopped.

Since our country's forestry has fallen into a state of depression due to various reasons, the remedies, at least, are systems that cultivate talents with forestry administration, as mentioned earlier. If we do not pay attention to this, then there is no hope for the revival of forestry. I have always admired the Indian forestry of the British, with the merits of Mr. Schlich being well-known. The forests of the United States were founded by Mr. Fernow, and the rapid progress of Japanese forestry was guided by Mr. Matsuno, whose great achievements are still in people's minds today. Is there no one in our forestry industry willing to work hard to build and break this depression? What I say here is not intended to imitate the Japanese forestry scholars' criticism of the government, complaining about the current world. I hope those who can redeem the situation will understand. (End)

Palestine: Jewish-Arab Conflict Evolves into Political Action; Arabs Implement Strikes and Boycotts 67

Jerusalem: The conflict between Jews and Arabs here has been ongoing for days. It began as religious fervor that evolved into riots with ethnic strife characteristics. However, it has now gradually evolved into purely political action. For example, the strike is backed by unions and mass gatherings, which are strictly controlled and directed. It is evident that this was pre-planned. As with the strike, other riots are also similar. However, officials have issued warnings to Arab leaders that further riots will be met with military suppression. This warning prevented a large-scale demonstration. Currently, the tragedy of armed conflict between Jews and Arabs seems unlikely, but the situation remains serious. The strike, initially expected to end quickly, is now likely to be prolonged and without a solution in sight. Arab leaders met all day today to discuss the situation, focusing primarily on the issues of continuing the strike and anti-Jewish strife. They did not adjourn until 8 p.m. It is reported that the Arabs have formed a high-level committee dedicated to enforcing the leaders' orders and coordinating the strike's forces. Within the province, incidents continue to occur, and unrest persists. In Tulkarm, a violent riot was followed by a serious demonstration, but authorities effectively prevented it from escalating. In Beisan and Nahalal, Arab arsonists burned crops in the fields. (Havas, 25th)

Jerusalem: A special report from our correspondent states that after the Arabs declared strikes and boycotts, agriculture has spread throughout Palestine. The streets are sparsely populated with vehicles, and shops are closed, creating a desolate scene, as if the entire city is on holiday. (Havas, 26th)

Jerusalem: A special report from our correspondent states that Arab leaders held a meeting yesterday and decided to adopt extraordinary measures to force people to accept the decision to strike and boycott. They also decided to set fire to any shops that remain open and, if necessary, to order schools to close. A major fire recently occurred in the Old City of Jerusalem. In addition, the Arab Higher Committee (headed by the Grand Mufti) has decided to put forward three minimum conditions for resolving the conflict: Immediate prohibition of Jewish immigration to Palestine; Prohibition of land sales to Jews; and Formation of an Arab national government. The Jewish Telegraphic Agency has issued a statement to Jews in Palestine and around the world, detailing the nation's construction efforts in Palestine, stating that they will continue this work fearlessly. (Havas, 26th)

Japanese-Soviet Negotiations: Resolving Border Disputes; Arita Proposes Eastern Demarcation Committee; Soviets Say Peaceful Atmosphere Needed Throughout 68

(Moscow) According to sources here, the first conversation between Japanese Foreign Minister Arita and Soviet Ambassador to Japan Yurenev focused solely on the organization of the border commission. Foreign Minister Arita stated that he does not oppose the organization of a commission for the entire Manchurian-Soviet border in principle, but under current circumstances, a committee to redraw the boundary line and resolve border disputes can only be established in the eastern part of the border.

The Soviet Ambassador replied that although the facts regarding the border issue are already very clear, the Soviet Union is still prepared to accept the Japanese government's proposal to establish a demarcation committee in the east, but a strong atmosphere of peace must exist throughout the entire border. In addition, the Soviet Ambassador also drew the Japanese Foreign Minister's attention to the importance of organizing similar committees for Outer Mongolia and Manchukuo.

Foreign Minister Arita replied that although the establishment of such a committee is necessary, this issue is not directly related to Japan. Therefore, under current circumstances, only a demarcation committee needs to be established on the eastern border. Foreign Minister Arita also asked the Soviet Ambassador to convey his views to the Soviet government and hoped for an early response from the Soviet authorities. The Soviet Ambassador immediately agreed to convey the Japanese government's views but immediately pointed out that a peaceful atmosphere should be promulgated throughout the entire border, not just in one part. (TASS, 25th)

(Moscow) On the 22nd of this month, Japanese Ambassador to Russia Ota hosted a farewell banquet for the former Japanese military attache at the Soviet Embassy, and a welcome reception for the newly appointed military attache. The Chairman of the Defense Committee, Voroshilov, Yegorov, and other key Soviet figures were in attendance. Ota delivered a speech saying that although there are various misunderstandings between Japan and the Soviet Union, they can all be resolved peacefully. Therefore, he strongly agreed with the statement made by the Chairman of the Soviet Defense Committee, "The Soviet Union is not afraid of war, but does not want to see war break out." The Japanese government is also seeking peace and avoiding war. If the current economic problems can be resolved, the relationship between the two countries will inevitably become closer.

Subsequently, the Chairman of the Soviet Defense Committee, Voroshilov, replied, "I strongly agree with the views of the Japanese Ambassador, because there is nothing that cannot be resolved between Japan and the Soviet Union. Furthermore, the Soviet government not only wishes to live in peace, but also strives for world peace. Therefore, it has previously requested to sign a non-aggression treaty to peacefully resolve various border disputes. However, border conflicts have increased in recent months. Although these conflicts are by no means provoked by the Red Army and border guards, their results will inevitably make the relationship between the two countries worse. Therefore, the Soviet government hopes that if the Japanese government is sincere in its efforts for peace, it must immediately stop the provocative actions of irresponsible personnel. The Soviet Union's unchanging policy of peace often leads to incorrect perceptions, believing that the Soviet government is cowardly. Mr. Hata is about to return home to take up the post of Director of the Intelligence Department of the Military Affairs Bureau. I (Voroshilov) sincerely hope that Mr. Hata will use his personal status to truthfully inform the Japanese people of the correct information and the truth that the Soviet Union loves peace."

Foreign Minister Arita: Clarifying Diplomatic Policy; Avoiding Provocative Actions Towards the Soviet Union; Greatly Influencing Domestic and Foreign Affairs 69

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Arita intends to clarify the direction of Japanese diplomatic policy in a speech to the special parliament. However, given the widespread rumors of an impending Japanese-Soviet war and the promotion of a Japanese-German alliance, he invited forty members of the newly formed foreign press corps from the United Kingdom, the United States, France, Germany, Italy, Russia, and other countries to his official residence at the Foreign Ministry on the 15th to discuss and clarify Japan's concrete diplomatic strategies. He specifically denied any provocative actions on the Japanese side regarding the Japanese-Soviet conflict and stated that a Japanese-German alliance was not under consideration, which greatly influenced domestic and foreign affairs. Japanese Financial Policy: Controlling National Financial Institutions; Thoroughly Improving Rural Economy 70

(Tokyo) Finance Minister Baba will deliver a financial speech in parliament. The relevant departments are currently drafting a concrete plan. It is understood that the general direction of economic policy is as follows:

(1) Improving Financial Institutions: Mobilizing special banks such as the Hypothec Bank of Japan and the Agricultural and Industrial Bank to thoroughly improve rural villages and rural finance. The goal is to establish rural financial institutions that do not aim to profit. General private banks should also act as public institutions to fulfill their mission and strengthen control. At the same time, the government should consider a guarantee system for the active activities of financial institutions in the industrial sector.

(2) Public Debt Policy: Improving financial and economic policies to increase the digestion of public bonds is a given. However, at times, the government may force savings banks, various government mutual aid organizations, and other financial institutions to purchase public bonds to expand their legislative means.

(3) Interest Rate Policy: The administrative power over banks, trust companies, unlimited credit organizations, insurance companies, etc., under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Finance should be transferred to the Ministry of Finance as much as possible. If transfer is not possible, close contact should be maintained with these financial institutions to thoroughly lower interest rates and promote the development of industry and trade. Implementation should be gradual, avoiding malicious inflation. At the same time, the economic repercussions and interest rate policies resulting from tax increases should be appropriately adjusted. (Domei, 26th)

Chairman Chiang's Speech: The Bright Path for the People of Sichuan (Continued) — At the Provincial Party Headquarters' Extended Commemoration Week — 76

Tenth, "Helping others is the root of happiness." We, as human beings, naturally seek happiness, but if we seek it in the wrong way, we will only find pain and create evil. For example, some people think that idle amusement, gambling, and dissipation are happiness, not knowing that these things are not only not happiness but also waste our energy, destroy our lives, increase our sins, and cause pain. They do not know that the greatest happiness of the human heart is to help others. The ancients said, "The more one does for others, the more one has for oneself; the more one gives to others, the more one receives." They also said, "Doing good is the greatest joy," meaning that the more we can help others, the more beneficial it is for us, and the happier we will be. There is a tenet of the Boy Scouts, "Do a good deed every day," which is also to help others. For example, rescuing from drowning, putting out fires, helping the elderly, protecting the young, and assisting the poor, hungry, injured, and sick—no matter how small the deed, it is doing good. Doing good can bring true happiness. All compatriots of the Republic of China should seek happiness in this way, loving each other and helping each other. As long as we have a bit of strength, we must do our best to help our compatriots. This is great happiness.

Eleventh, "Knowledge is the root of serving the world." This means that we must have knowledge and ability to serve the world and save the people, as Dr. Sun Yat-sen said, "The foundation of revolution lies in profound knowledge." On the other hand, it also means that the purpose of our studying all kinds of knowledge and skills is to serve the world and save people, not without purpose or meaning, not for personal comfort and security, and even less for using knowledge and skills to harm others and benefit ourselves, to commit evil acts. That serving the world requires knowledge, and that knowledge is the principle of serving the world, should already be clear to everyone. In particular, educators must thoroughly explain this to young students.

Twelfth, "Perseverance is the root of success." We all hope to be successful and achieve something in our lives. What is the most important condition for success? It is perseverance. Whatever we do, we must continue to work hard, not give up halfway or be fickle. We must have a beginning and an end, and see it through to the end. Especially if we want to succeed in a lifelong career, we must choose a bright and righteous path, strive forward, and never change until death, fulfilling the last two sentences of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will, "With one heart and one mind, persevere from beginning to end." For example, building a road—if we don't build it, we don't build it; but if we build it, we must build it all the way from the starting point to the ending point. No matter how many obstacles there are along the way, we must break through them until the entire route is connected. It should not be like the past situation in Sichuan, where a section is built in the east and another in the west. Before route A is completed, route B is started. As a result, although many sections are built, no road is completed. Such construction, even if it is a thousand sections or ten thousand miles, is useless. Therefore, whether we build roads or do any other large or small undertaking, we must always persevere, always be thorough, and always connect, which means we must constantly strive to improve ourselves, see it through to the end, and only then can we achieve true success.

The twelve principles mentioned above are the fundamental keys to our success in life and work, and the precious rafts for our revolution and nation-building. Today, I especially offer them to all comrades and compatriots in Sichuan. I hope that in the future, parents will use them to teach their children, officials will use them to teach their subordinates, and the government will use them to teach the people, so that all compatriots in Sichuan can put these twelve principles into practice. If so, I believe that the progress of Sichuan and the entire country will be rapid and unlimited. Finally, I have a few words to add about the matter of compulsory labor. Now, people generally know that the method of labor service is very beneficial to the people's physical and mental health and the order of society, so there is probably no doubt about it. However, there are many misunderstandings and complaints about the method of compulsory labor, especially in Sichuan. Originally, after a country or a place is restored to order and is in the midst of difficult construction, to universally mobilize the people to undertake any new cause, even if it is a cause that is very beneficial to the national economy and the people's livelihood and is very closely related, at first, the people always feel inconvenient and inevitably have complaints. Not to mention compulsory labor, which is a laborious task, even when the government wants to interfere with ordinary and minor matters such as public sanitation and cleanliness, the people will initially feel inconvenienced and harbor resentment. Especially when a new system is implemented, because of inadequate planning, incomplete personnel, lack of experience, etc., it is inevitable that malpractices will occur, making it all the more difficult for the people to feel pain and have complaints. This all depends on the government authorities and those who are responsible for education to consider the situation and guide them effectively. As for the matter of compulsory labor, it should originally be done during the slack season of farming so that the people can have time to work. Especially during the busy spring farming season, we should take into account the people's livelihood and sympathize with their suffering. Therefore, I have decided to issue an order that, except for the Sichuan-Hunan Highway, which must continue to requisition labor for construction due to special circumstances, the compulsory labor on all other roads will be suspended for one month. However, the people of Sichuan should know that compulsory labor is not limited to road construction. In the future, projects that are beneficial to the national economy and the people's livelihood, such as dredging rivers, afforestation, and building dikes, will all require labor. Our labor will never be wronged or difficult. Our labor service for the country and society is to create blessings for ourselves and our descendants. For example, after the highway is completed, not only can bandits be suppressed and the people can live and work in peace and contentment forever, but also progress and development can be achieved in all aspects of the economy, culture, and education, which will be of great benefit. We hope that all intellectuals will be responsible for educating the people in various ways so that they can understand, enjoy labor service, help others, and serve the world. I had a special feeling when I took a cargo ship from Hubei to Sichuan, which was to see the towering mountains of the Three Gorges. Yu the Great was able to dredge them by human power thousands of years ago. At that time, I really did not know how much effort your Sichuan ancestors had put in and how much blood and sweat they had shed. I think that such a difficult water conservancy project, in the era before machines were invented, and to succeed in such a great industry, the number of conscripted laborers who starved and froze to death was countless, and the number of people who were drowned for this dredging of the river was unknown to be thousands or tens of thousands of lives. From this, it can be seen that you Sichuan people not only have the ability to do great labor and construction, but also have the spirit of sacrificing oneself to benefit others, forgetting oneself for the sake of the public, and creating boundless welfare for future generations. Everyone, please think about it, if the Sichuan people's predecessors had not been able to exert the ability of labor service and the spirit of sacrificing everything to dredge the Three Gorges and channel the river, I am afraid that Sichuan would still be a world of wild beasts, and we would still be able to live and work in peace and contentment there. Since your Sichuan ancestors were able to dredge the towering mountains of the Three Gorges and create blessings for our future generations, do the current Sichuan people not have the ability to build a few highways? What is so strange about this small matter of road construction that it is worth complaining about? We cannot restore the inherent spirit of our ancestors and strive to improve ourselves, so we are not worthy of being the descendants of the Chinese nation, and we are also ashamed to be Sichuan people. I sincerely hope that in the future, the people of Sichuan must carry forward the great spirit of labor service of their ancestors, create boundless happiness for the country, for their compatriots, and for future generations, and complete the basic cause of revolution and nation-building with your Sichuan people's great spirit and courage, creating a permanently glorious history for the people of Sichuan. (End)

The First Phase of the Alberta Province's Three-Year Plan Completed: Entering the Stage of Ten New Constructions; Second Phase of the Plan About to Commence 77

Guangzhou Correspondence: After the Guangdong Province promulgated the Three-Year Administration Plan in June of the 21st year of the Republic [1932], it was decided to commence implementation on January 1st of the 22nd year [1933]. Now that the three-year term is complete, the Guangdong authorities have decided to continue to revise the second phase of the Three-Year Plan, designating the first half of this year as a period of assessment and investigation. This involves reviewing the progress of past work and investigating the actual needs of the current social environment to determine the second phase of the Three-Year Plan. Currently, in addition to relevant agencies submitting detailed reports on the implementation of the past plan, the heads of the Civil Affairs, Finance, Education, and Construction Departments have all recently made inspection tours to various counties to conduct on-the-ground investigations and broad consultations, using these findings as reference for drafting the second phase of the Three-Year Plan. As for the achievements of the first phase of the Three-Year Administration Plan, they already possess considerable value, as the plan represents a systematic approach to governance by the local government, stipulating various administrative procedures to enable cooperation among different sectors for step-by-step implementation. The aim is to build a new Guangdong in terms of politics, economy, education, and construction. Moreover, these plans are based on the platform and policies of the Kuomintang. The personnel responsible within the authorities possess a spirit of hard work and progress, leading to numerous achievements. An overview from various perspectives is as follows:

Political Aspect: Politically, it is easy to see significant achievements in public security. Guangdong has historically been a region where bandits gathered, especially in areas such as Guangzhou Bay, which were governed by foreigners. This facilitated the smuggling of arms, indirectly creating opportunities for bandit activity. Bandits often established affiliations, kidnapped people for ransom, looted in all directions, and extorted fees, causing havoc for three to four decades. Furthermore, Haifeng, Lufeng, Qiongyai, Suyang, and Huilai Kunyun Nanshan, among other places, were occupied by Red bandits [Communists]. The mutual collusion of Red and ordinary bandits became a major disaster in Guangdong Province. However, after the implementation of the Three-Year Administration Plan, five pacification zones were delineated, each with a dedicated commissioner responsible for pacification. At the same time, local guard teams were actively organized to strengthen local defense capabilities. Consequently, not only were the Communist bandits within the territory suppressed, but various bandit gangs were also wiped out. Currently, the people live in peace, and commerce is unhindered, which is considered by the people of Guangdong to be the most satisfactory and commendable achievement. Moreover, the corruption among Guangdong officials was historically more severe than in any other province, a deeply entrenched problem since the late Qing Dynasty. However, in the past two to three years, there has been some change. First, the highest authorities have shown considerable determination in rectifying officialdom. Second, the heads of county finance bureaus are directly appointed by the provincial finance department, making them not personal associates of the county magistrate and thus less susceptible to corruption. Third, the Department of Civil Affairs regularly sends personnel to conduct inspections. If evidence of corruption is discovered, strict punishment is swiftly meted out. Consequently, there have been numerous cases in the past two to three years of county magistrates being dismissed, detained, and even executed for corruption, leading to a transformation in the ethos of officialdom.

Financial Aspect: Guangdong was originally known as a wealthy region, so the finances of Guangdong should have been quite affluent. In reality, the economy of Guangdong relies heavily on remittances from overseas Chinese and exports of raw silk as its two main pillars. In recent years, it has been affected by the global economic downturn. The price of raw silk has plummeted, and remittances from overseas Chinese have also shrunk, naturally leading to a reduction in various tax revenues. The finances of Guangdong have therefore faced considerable difficulties. However, the Guangdong authorities have not sought improper sources of income or increased taxes. Instead, they have cut more than 120 types of harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies, amounting to a total of over 6 million silver dollars per year. Administrative expenses have been paid at 80%, and measures have been taken to eliminate corruption and embezzlement in financial matters to increase public revenue. After two to four reorganizations, the monthly salary amount has also increased by over 30,000 silver dollars. In this way, the finances of Guangdong can still be sustained. As for abolishing land taxes and switching to land value taxes, the aim is to reduce the long-standing problems of having land without taxes, having taxes without land, and embezzlement in household registration, which demonstrates considerable diligence. The transition to land value taxes is now almost complete. However, there are also many problems here. Instead of relying on people's reported land value for taxation, an evaluation committee is organized to assess land prices for taxation. Land varies in fertility and accessibility. A slight oversight can easily lead to disputes. It is reported that the government is in the process of adjusting. Second, after the conversion to land value tax, all land tax surcharges are supposed to be eliminated, but some places still retain many surcharges, which in turn increases the burden on the people. The government has recently issued a clear order prohibiting the private collection of land tax surcharges.

Educational Aspect: In the past two to three years, the education authorities have placed great emphasis on promoting compulsory education and vocational education, which is very suitable for the actual requirements of China's environment. The extent of progress can be illustrated by statistical figures. In the 20th year of the Republic [1931], there were 18,969 elementary schools in the province, with 1,098,926 students. By the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], there were 22,754 elementary schools, with 1,469,401 students. Education expenditure paid by the provincial treasury (excluding local funds) was 2,134,425 yuan in the 19th year of the Republic [1930]. By the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], it had increased to 4,332,270 yuan, nearly doubling. In the 24th year of the Republic [1935], an additional 100,600 yuan was added to expand secondary school classes, and over 350,000 yuan was newly established for vocational and normal schools. Subsidies were provided to various counties for running short-term elementary schools and increasing compulsory education, totaling 250,000 yuan (including 120,000 yuan in central government subsidies). This is an additional 700,000 yuan. In recent years, Guangdong's financial revenue has decreased, while education expenditure has increased annually, demonstrating the great effort exerted by the education administration.

Construction Aspect: The Guangdong government has decided to manage major industries with government financial resources. In the Three-Year Administration Plan, there were plans to establish cotton mills, silk weaving factories, woolen mills, jute textile mills, sulfuric acid and soda factories, phosphate fertilizer plants, nitrogen fertilizer plants, paper mills, sugar mills, alcohol distilleries, refined salt manufacturing plants, corn alcohol distilleries, insecticide manufacturing plants, Xisha Islands guano fertilizer manufacturing plants, vegetable oil oleic acid factories, oil manufacturing plants, Shanwei aquatic product manufacturing plants, mechanized peanut oil factories, improved agricultural tool manufacturing plants, fishing boat manufacturing plants, new fishing gear manufacturing plants, steel plants, and the Wengjiang hydroelectric power plant, totaling 24 factories. Of these, the alcohol distillery, sulfuric acid factory, soda factory, wood charcoal automobile factory, silk weaving and woolen textile mills, cotton mills, jute textile mills, nitrogen fertilizer plant, phosphate fertilizer plant, and sugar mill have already been established. The paper mill, steel plant, and Wengjiang hydroelectric power plant are in preparation but have not yet been established. The established factories all have products, the trademark being "Five Years Brand", with a management office in Shanghai for promotion. Among these, sugar has been the most successful, because Guangdong's land and climate are particularly suitable for growing sugarcane. In the past, when sugar was produced by traditional methods, there were over 10 million yuan in native sugar exports. Later, after the intrusion of machine-made foreign sugar, the native sugar gradually declined, and ordinary farmers could not maintain their livelihoods. Therefore, the Guangdong government resolutely established factories and purchased machinery to squeeze sugarcane in the Three-Year Plan. The sugar produced is no different from foreign sugar. Since then, not only has the import of foreign sugar decreased, but the sugar produced can also be sold throughout the country. The provincial government believes that sugarcane sugar has great potential and is actively expanding it. It has now planned to establish ten major sugar factories throughout the province. Currently, the Panyu Xinzhao and Shitou factories, Jieyang factory, Huiyang factory, and Shunde factory are in production. The Dongguan factory, Nanlu Haikang factory, and Qiongyai factory are in preparation. The plan for ten major sugar factories will not be difficult to realize in the future. However, the raw material of sugarcane may not be sufficient in the future. Currently, only five factories have been completed, and the supply of raw materials is already facing difficulties. If ten major sugar factories are established one after another, what will be the supply of raw materials? This is not an easy problem to solve. Although the government has a plan for developing rural areas in the Three-Year Plan and has decided to convert some mulberry fields into sugarcane fields and reclaim wasteland for planting sugarcane, as well as provide low-interest loans to farmers for planting sugarcane, and has contacted the Shanghai Bank in Shanghai to allocate 1.4 million yuan for handling freight loans in Guangdong branches, this may not be able to solve the problem. In fact, sugarcane planting is not suitable for newly reclaimed wasteland, and there is not so much mature land. If rice fields are converted, it will affect the problem of people's food. If rapid success is desired, the government must find a way to improve the soil of newly reclaimed wasteland, because this is not something that ordinary farmers can do.

Rural Aspect: Rural areas have suffered due to the decline in raw silk exports and the reduction in remittances from overseas Chinese. Small industries, such as the tobacco from Heshan, oranges from Xinhui, tangerines from Xinhui, and the sunflower fans from Gaoyao, have all experienced reduced exports, affecting rural poverty. All industrial and commercial enterprises have become sluggish. Fortunately, in recent years, due to political stability, there have been no wars or bandit disasters. In particular, the government has reduced 120 kinds of harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies, which has reduced the burden on rural areas and alleviated some of the difficulties. It is reported that the government has considered many ways to alleviate poverty in rural areas. The first phase of the Three-Year Plan also included a rural construction plan, but the results were very small. The main reasons are: first, water conservancy is not developed; second, rural areas are poor; third, the production technology of farmers is poor. If a serious large-scale effort is made, a huge amount of funds will naturally be needed, but this is not possible with the current financial resources. If it is transformed bit by bit, the effect will naturally be weak. Therefore, the Guangdong authorities are making efforts in the face of difficulties, such as the establishment of rural cooperatives, the establishment of rural loans, the establishment of agricultural schools, the improvement of silk and agricultural crops, and are doing their best. It is also reported that large-scale water conservancy projects will be carried out in the second phase of the Three-Year Plan, so it is expected that considerable success will be achieved in rural construction.

Chen Jitang Sends Personnel to Investigate the Construction of Guangxi Province; Various Agencies Jointly Form an Inspection Delegation to Guangxi Province to Provide Reference for the Second Phase of the Three-Year Plan 78

Guangzhou Correspondence: In recent years, Guangxi Province has made considerable progress in all aspects of construction. Chen Jitang, Director of the Guangzhou Pacification Headquarters, has specially ordered his subordinates to organize an inspection delegation to Guangxi Province to conduct on-the-ground investigations of various undertakings for reference. He has designated Feng Zhuoxun, Chief of the Guard of the Guangdong Headquarters, as the team leader. As for the members, they will be senior officials sent by various agencies. In addition to several people sent by the headquarters, the Pacification Headquarters of the Eastern District, Southern District, Qiongyai District, Northwest District, and Central District, as well as the Departments of Civil Affairs, Finance, Construction, and Education, will each send one person to jointly organize the delegation. The members of the delegation are ready to depart, awaiting Chen's scheduled convocation and briefing before setting off. The itinerary is to first go to Wuzhou, and then take a highway bus directly to Nanning, the capital of Guangxi Province, and visit Guilin, Bose, Liuzhou, and other counties for inspection on a daily basis. It has also been found that the Guangxi Provincial People's Militia is organized very comprehensively, equivalent to the Guangdong Provincial Guard, assisting the garrison in peacetime, searching and suppressing bandits with extraordinary effectiveness, and able to rise up to defend the territory and protect the locality in times of need. In order to make the Guangdong Provincial Guard a purely civilian military force, Chen has established an office to coordinate its management. Recently, he has divided the province into 16 guard inspection districts, each with an inspection commissioner to specialize in management. Seven commissioners have been appointed and transferred to a military and political school for a month of apprenticeship before being sent out to serve. In view of the considerable success of the Guangxi Provincial People's Militia, the inspection delegation has been ordered to pay special attention to this matter, so that it can be used as a reference when reviewing the second phase of the province's Three-Year Administration Plan. It is also found that the delegation can set off in three to four days and return to Guangdong to report in three weeks.

Gansu Provincial Government to Undertake Seven Construction Projects; Prohibiting the Slaughter of Pregnant Sheep to Propagate Livestock 79

Lanzhou Correspondence: Recently, the provincial government has been very active in various construction undertakings, and has planned work on a monthly basis to proceed step by step. As for those to be undertaken this month, Provincial Government Chairman Yu instructed the Department of Construction to properly draft and submit them for review, and they have been implemented separately, including highways, water conservancy, and electricity, among other seven items, all of which are extremely important. The outline is as follows: (1) Highway aspect: Construct the Gansu-Qinghai-Taoqin Highway, measure the second main line of the Gansu-Sichuan Road, measure the main line of the Gansu-Xinjiang Road, construct the Qingshui-Zhangjiachuan branch road, and construct the Sijiahe Bridge in conjunction with Shaanxi Province; (2) Water conservancy aspect: Construct the Tao-Hui Canal, conduct an actual measurement of the Xingu City Canal, construct the Tiaocheng Yellow River dike project, and repair the Jingyuan Beihai River project; (3) Electricity aspect: Set up rural telephone networks in Qingyang, He, Huan, Ning, Zheng, and Jingchuan counties, and repair the Lanzhou electric light boiler; (4) Agricultural aspect: Distribute cotton seeds and promote cotton planting; (5) Forestry aspect: Universal afforestation and establishment of nurseries; (6) Measurements aspect: Promote measurement instruments. Chairman Yu of the Provincial Government stated that people in various counties often arbitrarily slaughter pregnant sheep and sell them on the market or eat them themselves, which affects the propagation of livestock. In order to prevent harm to livestock breeding, he has specifically formulated the "Measures for Punishing People in Gansu Province for Slaughtering Pregnant Sheep," consisting of seven articles, which have been promulgated and circulated to all county bureaus for compliance and prohibition. (24th day)

Songjiang Organizes Bandit Suppression Guerrilla Detachment 80

According to a report from Zhao Zanchen, commander of the 12th Brigade, to Wang Gongying, Security Commander of the Third District, bandits are appearing and disappearing unpredictably in Punan and along the coast, making suppression necessary to curb chaos. After receiving the order, Zhao rushed to inspect the Beiqiao area on the 16th. Investigation of Extortion Letter 81

Lou Youzhong, a villager from the 9th Jia of the 6th Bao of Beicheng Township in the 5th District (Fengjing), had a hole dug in his wall on the night of the 13th of March, but the thieves escaped without any loss due to the victim's shouting. However, when Lou went to town to shop on the 18th, he met Zhang Zixian from the same village on the way to Dongzhakou. Zhang gave Lou a letter. As Lou could not read, he asked someone to open it. It turned out to be a threatening letter from the thieves, which roughly stated that seven people had hired a boat the previous night and lost ten yuan, eight jiao, and five fen. It instructed Lou to admit the loss and compensate for the loss, or they would be unfavorable to him. They would come to collect on the first day of the third lunar month. Lou was greatly alarmed and asked Jia Chang Lou Youxian to report it to the Second Sub-Bureau, which arrested Zhang Zixian. He was sent to the Public Security Bureau on the 26th for interrogation.

The county government recently decided to build a meteorological observatory on the top of Ma'anshan Mountain and has ordered the section to draw up a detailed plan. It is estimated that it will cost more than 3,000 yuan. The architectural drawings have also been drawn up and are now being submitted for approval. Once approved, bids will be invited for construction. Li Zhengyi, a farmer from Yancun Township outside Xiaoximen in the first district of the county, suddenly suffered a stroke on the afternoon of the 25th. He asked Jin, an elderly man in the neighborhood, to draw out the sickness. However, as soon as the needle was inserted into his abdomen, it broke in half. The family was extremely anxious and sent him to the county hospital for treatment, but the needle could not be extracted. His life is in danger.

Wuxi Villagers Shed Blood in Investigative Court 84

Tang Rongfu, Tang Zhida, and others, villagers from Chengtang Township in Guanhui Township in the 5th District of the county, recently built houses and built walls. However, Tang Jingliu, Tang Shunbao, Tang Chenshi, and others, who were Manchus, went to stop them and destroyed the walls. Tang and others then filed a complaint with the local court against Tang Shunbao for property damage. On the previous day, Tang Jingliu's younger brother went to obstruct them again, resulting in a conflict with Tang Rongfu, with both sides sustaining minor injuries. Tang Zhida's mother went to the court to show her injuries. Yesterday morning, Tang Jingliu also hired lawyer Jiang Gongjian to draft a statement requesting the local court to examine his mother's injuries. After an interrogatory examination by Prosecutor Ren, they were instructed to return and await a field examination. However, Tang Jingliu was eager for the judge to go to the countryside and suddenly had a nervous breakdown. He took out a copper book pillow from his pocket and hit his head wildly in court, causing blood to flow like a madman. The judge was also shocked and immediately adjourned the court. Shortly after, the court resumed. Tang Jingliu was temporarily admitted to the hospital. In the afternoon, they went to the countryside for examination. Tang Zhangshi, who fell, was also not seriously injured. Prosecutor Ren immediately opened a court to question him, stating that Tang Jingliu had obstructed official business and ordered him to be released on bail pending further investigation.

Haizhou: Heavy Rains Cause Disaster and Another Year of Famine. Since last year's Yellow River flowed eastward and flooded, most farmers in the county were without clothes or food, and the disaster was severe, unprecedented in decades. When the Yellow River receded this spring, farmers borrowed high-interest loans and received government allocations for relief to sow spring wheat. Now that the wheat seedlings are growing, it has been raining heavily for several days, and the water level in the flat areas of the villages is more than a foot deep, submerging the wheat seedlings. This year's harvest is also hopeless, and farmers are generally worried.

Yesterday was the last day. Simultaneous lantern parades were held in the evening at both South Shanghai and Pudong. The situation is recorded as follows:

More than 50,000 people participated in the group. Spectators line the streets along the route. Wherever it passed, it was crowded with spectators like entering a mountain or the sea. In order to prevent petty criminals from taking advantage of the opportunity to cause trouble, the Municipal Party Department specially notified the Municipal Security Committee to instruct the Bao members of the South Shanghai Regiment Guard teams to be fully on duty along the route of the lantern parade last night, so the order was quite good.

Therefore, the Fifth District Party Department made preparations in advance and gathered thousands of people from various agencies and organizations at the vacant space of the Bing Tian Factory on Dongchang Road in Pudong at 6:00 pm last night to hold a lantern parade. The viewers blocked the road, which was quite eye-catching to the public.

The Public Security Bureau publishes notices to smokers. The Municipal Public Security Bureau, in order to awaken smokers to register as soon as possible, specially printed a notice to smokers and distributed it along the way. The original text is as follows: (1) The valid period of the first-term limited smoking cessation permit has expired. Smokers who have obtained a permit should quickly go to the Public Security Bureau to exchange for the second-term limited smoking cessation permit. (2) Smokers who have failed to register should quickly go to the Public Security Bureau to complete the registration and apply for a limited smoking cessation permit. (3) The deadline for smokers to report is a total of three months. Those who do not register within the reporting period will be immediately sent to a smoking cessation hospital for treatment without spending a penny. (4) Those who smoke opium without obtaining a limited smoking cessation permit will be handed over to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for punishment in accordance with military law if they are discovered by the Bureau after the deadline for smokers to report has passed.
