China Flying Society Will Open Flying Classes, Registration Deadline is the 15th of Next Month, Three Trainer Aircraft Assembled 91

Central News Agency reports that the China Flying Society Flying Class, after more than a year of preparation, has assembled all three trainer aircraft. The hangars and classrooms at Longhua Airport are under construction. The opening date is scheduled for the end of next month. Registration has now begun and will close on the 15th of next month. Male and female members are enthusiastically registering. The Society's brochure and curriculum are recorded as follows:

Key Points of the Brochure. The Flying Class Regulations have been approved by the government. The key points are as follows: (A) Qualifications: Applicants must meet the following requirements: A. Be a member of the Society; B. Be in good health and meet the Society's physical examination standards; C. Have a secondary education level; D. Be between 18 and 35 years old; E. Have a reliable guarantor. Registration procedures: Applicants must bring their membership badge and fee receipt to the Society to fill out the application form and submit three recent two-inch bareheaded frontal half-length photos. Physical examination: Designated doctors from the Society will conduct the examination according to the physical examination form. Examination: Examination subjects include Chinese, Arithmetic, Foreign Language, Physics, and Common National Knowledge. Enrollment procedures: A. Fill out a guarantee form; B. Pay tuition fees. Quota: The quota for the first term is tentatively set at 20 students. Tuition fees: The tuition fee for the entire term is 600 yuan (limited to the completion of the primary course). Duration of study: Each term is limited to six months (the duration of study may be extended if weather conditions prevent it). Withdrawal: Any member who meets one of the following conditions may be ordered to withdraw from the school: A. Significant changes in physical health occur during the course of study, making it impossible to continue learning to fly; B. Flying performance is poor, and it is not suitable for learning to fly; C. The member himself encounters a special environment and cannot continue flying, which has been verified and approved by the Society; D. Absence from class for a total of one month, which the Society considers to be unworthy of cultivation. For the above four items, except for the fourth item, the remaining one, two, and three items will have the tuition fees refunded proportionally to the number of flying lessons at the time of withdrawal. Study: During the study period, all flying clothing, flying equipment, and vehicles to and from flying will be provided by the Society. The examination will be supervised by personnel dispatched by the aviation authority and will be conducted in accordance with the flying personnel examination regulations.

Physical Standards. The Academy attaches great importance to physical fitness. Applicants must fill in the details of each part of the body on the form when registering. After passing the examination, the designated doctor will conduct a physical examination before admission is allowed. The stipulated physical standards are: Height: Men 63 inches or more, women 60 inches or more. Weight: Men 110 pounds or more, women 95 pounds or more. Chest circumference difference: 2 inches or more. No heart murmurs. Auscultation and percussion of the lungs: No pathological changes. No pterygium, severe trachoma, or other serious eye diseases. Visual acuity of each eye must be at least 1.0/2.0. Normal color vision. Each ear must be able to hear faint sounds at a distance of 20 feet. The eardrum must be completely free of perforations. The throat and tonsils must not have special swelling.

Curriculum Items. (A) Academic subjects: Flying techniques: 1. Principles of flight; 2. Flight maneuvers. Engineering: 1. Structure of lighter-than-air aircraft; 2. Structure of heavier-than-air aircraft. Mechanics: 1. Theory and practice of gas production; 2. Theory and practice of refrigeration; 3. Theory and practice of lubrication; 4. Theory and practice of ignition. Meteorology. Common National Knowledge. (B) Technical subjects: Straight flight. Large turns. Medium turns. Stall feel. Climbing turns. Gliding turns. Spirals. Ground taxiing. Takeoff. Landing. Route flight. Solo flight. Small turns. Angle turns (180 degrees) ascending turns. Figure-8 turns.

Central China Communications Bank, Ten Million Auxiliary Coins Enter Sichuan, Adjusting Finance, Activating Supply, Meeting Social Needs, Disaster Relief Loan Signed, Shanghai Bank Prepares to Pay 92

The Central China Communications and other three banks, in order to meet the needs of Sichuan Province, decided to transport 10 million yuan of auxiliary coin notes to Sichuan for use. The Sichuan Province Post-Disaster Public Bonds were used to mortgage a 620,000 yuan disaster relief loan to the Central and other three banks, which has been signed. The details of each situation are recorded as follows: Ten million auxiliary coins are transported to Sichuan for adjustment. The finance of Sichuan Province, since being taken over by Hang Chen of the Central Government, has been actively reorganized. Liu Hangchen actively reorganized, and the Central Government allocated a loan of 12 million yuan to adjust Sichuan's financial situation, and after recovering the unredeemed remittance certificates and local banknotes issued by various banks and shops in Chongqing, the finance has been on track. Since the implementation of the legal tender policy on November 4 last year, the province's finance has become more stable. However, the amount of legal tender circulating in Sichuan Province is still insufficient, and Director Liu has often reported to Finance Minister Kong and requested that more legal tender be transported to Sichuan to facilitate turnover. The Ministry of Finance immediately ordered the Central and other three banks to transport 10 million yuan of auxiliary coins to Sichuan for use. The auxiliary coins are divided into 1 jiao, 2 jiao, and 5 jiao, with the Central Bank having the most. They have been transported from Shanghai to Chongqing by Minsheng Shipping. It is scheduled to transport 5 million yuan within the month, and the remaining 5 million yuan will be transported next month. Therefore, after Sichuan Province increases by 10 million auxiliary coins, the financial market can become more active.

The contract is signed, and a telegram is sent to Shanghai to release the funds. In order to handle disaster relief matters in Sichuan Province, Liu Hangchen, Director of the Department of Finance of Sichuan Province, came to Shanghai in mid-March to visit Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Finance and President of the Central Bank, and Song Ziwen, Chairman of the Bank of China, etc., and agreed on the principle of mortgaging post-disaster public bonds to borrow funds, and then returned to Chongqing, and contacted various branches. After deliberation, it was agreed to mortgage 1 million yuan of post-disaster public bonds for a loan of 620,000 yuan, which would be jointly recognized by the Central China Chinese Farmers' Three Banks for 310,000 yuan, and the silver and money industry in Chongqing would jointly recognize 310,000 yuan, totaling 620,000 yuan. The contract was signed in Chongqing on the 25th. The Central China Chinese Farmers' and other sub-branches have all telegraphed Shanghai to report on the signing process and urge the release of funds. After receiving the telegram, the three banks decided to remit the funds to Chongqing within days and pay them to the Sichuan Finance Department to meet their needs.

Since the Central China Communications Bank was ordered by the Ministry of Finance to exercise legal tender, domestic and foreign finance has relied on the three banks to regulate. In addition to actively assisting finance in various places, they will temporarily suspend the establishment of branch offices in places where three bank branches are currently located. Otherwise, they will immediately set up offices or branch offices according to the history of the three banks. As for the headquarters of the Central Bank, it was established on November 1, 17th year of the Republic, and there are currently 8 branch offices in Nanjing and other places, 15 second-class branch offices in Qingdao and other places, and 4 third-class branch offices in Zhenjiang and other places. In addition, there are 18 offices affiliated with the first and second-class branch offices. There are currently 164 head and branch offices. In addition to the recent establishment of branch offices and offices in the United Kingdom, new branch offices in Singapore and other places will be completed this year. The headquarters of the Communications Bank was established in December of the 33rd year of Guangxu in the late Qing Dynasty. There are currently 105 head and branch offices. Recently, branch offices will be established in Shantou and other places. In summary, the three banks currently have 315 head and branch offices.

Zhejiang Public Bonds of 60 Million to be Issued on May 1, Director of the Department of Finance Comes to Shanghai to Consult with the Silver and Money Industry on Mortgages, Visited Beijing Yesterday to Negotiate with the Legislative Yuan, and Passage is Expected 94

The Zhejiang Provincial Government is issuing 60 million yuan of unified public bonds to reorganize old debts, which is approved for issuance on May 1. Cheng Yuanfan, Director of the Department of Finance, came to Shanghai the day before yesterday to discuss mortgage matters with the Shanghai banking community, and visited Beijing yesterday to consult with the Legislative Yuan. Details are recorded as follows:

Issuing new bonds to replace old debts. The Zhejiang Provincial Government is issuing 60 million yuan of unified public bonds to reorganize old debts due to financial difficulties. It has been approved by the Executive Yuan. The public bonds are purely for replacing previously issued debts, repaying old public bonds, highway public bonds, construction public bonds, disaster relief public bonds, clearing old debts, provincial gold military bonds, local public bonds, etc. They are divided into four types: A, B, C, and D. Type A is 4.5 million yuan, with a term of 14 years and an interest rate of 9%. Type B is 17 million yuan, with a term of 16 years and an interest rate of 7%. Type C is 10.5 million yuan, with a term of 18 years and an interest rate of 6%. Type D is 28 million yuan, with a term of 20 years and an interest rate of 6%. It is approved for issuance on May 1.

Director Cheng comes to Shanghai to discuss mortgages. Director Cheng has contacted the Zhejiang and Shanghai banking communities several times and has obtained their understanding. A reporter from the New Voice Agency specially visited Cheng yesterday. According to Cheng, the public bonds will be issued on May 1. Rumors that they will be issued on June 1 and that exchange vouchers will be issued first are not true. As for the Legislative Yuan, it is expected to pass the bill within days, so there is no problem. As for the Zhejiang Province's use of previously issued public bonds or treasury bills as collateral to borrow funds from the Shanghai-Hangzhou silver and money industry, the contract will be maintained as usual and will not be changed due to this. It is found that the Zhejiang Province's borrowing fraud totals 11,253,795 yuan, 5 jiao, 6 fen, and 1 li. After the new public bonds are issued, in addition to replacing the old public bonds and old military bonds, there will be a surplus. Director Cheng discussed mortgages with the China Communications, Siming, China Agricultural and Industrial, and Zhejiang Xingye Banks the day before yesterday and obtained their consent. He went to Beijing last night to consult with the Legislative Yuan.

Wusong Spring Fish on the Market, The First Batch of Three Fishing Boats Arrived in Wusong Yesterday, But All the Fish are Only for Local Entertainment 98

The spring fishing season in Wusong, namely the Beiyang yellow croaker, had the first batch of three fishing boats arriving yesterday. The various situations are recorded on the left.

Import situation. This year's spring fishing boats are quite numerous. However, due to the large wind and waves on the ocean surface, it is not easy to cast nets. Yesterday morning, the Gong He Shun, Jin Yuan Tai, and Jin Tong Zeng fishing boats successively imported. After inspection by the customs, they were unloaded ashore and sold by the joint office of the Cui Sheng, Shen Tai, and Guan Tai fish firms. The fixed price is 6 yuan and 6 jiao per 80 catties, and 14 catties of fish can be purchased per yuan. However, the goods that arrived yesterday can only be used for entertainment by local fish dealers. Therefore, local wholesale must wait for a large number of fishing boats to import.

Local Bureau Guarantee The various authorities pay great attention to the fishing season. In addition to issuing notices for protection, District Chief Dai Chenggong and Captain Wang Dingsheng from the Tax District sent teams to patrol the water surface. The Public Security Police Station added posts to maintain order on the Outer Bund.

Fish Firm Talk According to the person in charge of the fish firm, the fish market in Songdi has been declining year by year, and the business has decreased by two-thirds compared with the prosperous period in the past. Therefore, in recent years, the joint business of the three firms, including spring fish, turtle fish, and dried fish, has only about 200,000 yuan of business in total. The reason is that most fishing boats are sailing to Qingdao for sales. The salt price is cheaper in that place, and the transportation costs are reduced, so the fishing boats are turning north, which has greatly affected the Songdi fish firms.

Silver and Money Industry Tightens Lending Before the End of April, Deposits are Abundant, Foreign Interbank Lending Rates are Quietly Low, Preliminary Decision to Discuss Interest Rate Reduction in Early May 99

The industry news agency said that before the end of the April settlement period, the silver and money industry in the city suddenly tightened lending, resulting in abundant deposits and low foreign interbank lending rates. The issue of interest rate reduction is scheduled to be discussed again in early May. The details are explored and recorded as follows:

Tight Lending. The Banking Association and the Money Industry Association, in view of the fact that the Shanghai industrial and commercial industries in previous years have been in a slump due to the poor economic situation, rural bankruptcy, and weak purchasing power of the people, the economy has been deteriorating, so they have worked together to lend money for relief in order to revive the economy. However, by the end of April this year, it is actually difficult to fully recover the long-term loans granted to various industries, and there are quite a few who have declared liquidation and bankruptcy. In order to protect their own foundations, they unanimously implemented a tight policy before the end of April in order to maintain their business.

Low Foreign Interbank Lending Rates. In recent years, due to the sluggishness of various industries, the business of each money firm has also declined. Except for the Central China Communications Bank, whose business is growing day by day, the other commercial banks are not as good as before. Therefore, they are all extremely cautious about various loans, resulting in concentrated finance and no way out. During this annual extraordinary period at the end of April, the foreign interbank lending rate in the money industry market is still as low as 8%, which shows that the silver and money industry has sufficient preparations and can steadily weather the difficulties. However, the industrial and commercial industries have no access to loans, and the future is quite bleak.

Re-discuss Interest Rate Reduction. The Ministry of Finance previously approved the request of industry leaders in Shanghai and specially ordered the silver and money industries to formulate measures to reduce the interest rates on deposits and loans. After the two industries discussed and reported, the Ministry of Finance approved and ordered immediate reconsideration. According to news from the two industries yesterday, the Ministry of Finance could have agreed to the previous report, but due to the relationship of relieving the market, it had to order reconsideration. It is heard that the two industries will re-discuss interest rate reduction measures in early May and strive to realize them.

Goods Exported to Egypt: Certificates of Origin Should be Issued to Avoid Being Mistaken for Japanese Goods. The Ministry of Finance Orders all Customs Houses to Act Accordingly.

The Ministry of Finance has approved a request from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that goods from our country imported into Egypt are sometimes considered to be Japanese goods, and are subject to an additional 40% tax upon import. To ensure that goods exported to Egypt receive reliable certification, the Ministry requests that all customs houses across the country be instructed to handle the issuance of certificates of origin for goods exported to Egypt, in accordance with the regulations. After approving the request, the Ministry of Finance has already ordered all customs houses to comply.

Ministry of Industry Approves Trial Implementation of National Match Merchant Joint Venture and is Carefully Considering the Establishment of a Sino-Japanese Production and Sales Joint Venture.

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, in recent years, the establishment of match factories in our country has sprung up like mushrooms after rain, resulting in overproduction and slow sales. In order to develop the match business, limit the increase in production, and unify selling prices, the Shanghai China National Match Industry Association convened a general meeting of colleagues from factories across the country and resolved to organize a match joint venture to facilitate consolidation. A draft plan and articles of association have been submitted to the Ministry of Industry for approval. The joint venture has been approved by the Ministry for a five-year trial period. During the trial period, the establishment of new factories and the increase in production by existing factories will be suspended in order to maintain the common prosperity of the domestic match industry. In addition to uniting domestic match manufacturers to promote development, negotiations are being conducted with Japanese merchants to establish a Sino-Japanese match industry production and sales joint venture. This is because smuggling has become rampant recently and cannot be stopped. A large amount of smuggled goods are sold in the country, and our match industry is facing a thorny situation. Therefore, repeated discussions have been held with the Japanese side, and opinions are gradually converging. The outline of the plan has now been submitted to the Ministry of Industry for approval. The Ministry considers this matter to be related to the progress of the domestic match industry and of great importance, and that it is an international commercial joint organization, and must be carefully examined.

The internship of these staff members is about to expire in June of this year. In order to seek further study for the staff members, the Ministry of Communications has decided to allow them to be assigned to Germany for continued internship after completing their internships, until the end of August next year. From the beginning of September next year, the staff members will be allowed to take advantage of their return to the country and travel to Switzerland, France, England, Denmark, Russia, and other countries to visit and observe postal and remittance matters. They are limited to staying two weeks in Switzerland, three weeks each in France and England, one week in Denmark, and one week in Soviet Russia, including travel dates. At the beginning of October, the staff members will return to the country via the Siberian Railway. The list of training institutions and subjects to be studied in Germany, along with the list of subjects for observation and study in various countries, will be sent to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting them to forward it to the embassy in Germany to contact the German government, and to the embassies in various countries to contact the respective governments in advance.

Three Robbers Disregard the Law: Daring to Rob in Broad Daylight. A Wealthy Couple Loses Five or Six Hundred Yuan. Woman Injured in the Abdomen for Refusing to Give Up Handbag.

Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, a well-dressed and ornately adorned couple was riding in separate rickshaws near the Zhangjia Lane entrance in Xue Lane, downtown, when three or four robbers armed with pistols suddenly jumped out of the alley, ordering the rickshaw pullers to stop. One of the robbers pointed a pistol at the woman, warning her not to make a sound, while the other robbers stood guard outside the alley. The robbers took a gold bracelet from the woman's hand and hid it in their waistbands. However, the robbers' desires were not yet satisfied, and they wanted to take the handbag from the woman's hand as well. The husband, standing beside her, did not dare to speak and advised his wife to give up the handbag. But the woman insisted on refusing. The robbers, fearing that the delay would cause them to be discovered, quickly aimed their pistols at the woman's abdomen and fired a shot. The woman immediately fainted from the extreme pain, and the robbers grabbed the handbag and fled. The loss was five or six hundred yuan. Afterwards, her husband reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau, requesting a strict investigation and arrest of the perpetrators, and sent his injured wife to the hospital for treatment.

Japanese Sailor Murder Case: First Special Court Opens Joint Session Today Out of Caution.范剛 Designated to Defend the Three Defendants, Ye, Yang, and Chen. Hearing May Not Prohibit Public Attendance This Afternoon.

Following the murder of Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo on Date Street, the Japanese Consulate General apprehended a Korean named Jack, while the Public Concession's Special Political Department also apprehended three Cantonese suspects, Ye Haisheng (also known as "Little Guangdong") and two Chens, in Qingdao and elsewhere, based on various leads. They were handed over to the First Special District Court for detention. The details have been reported in the press. It is learned that the case was continued on the morning of the 27th of this month at the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court, presided over by Judge Xiao Xiefei. At that time, the Public Concession will file a public prosecution for murder. It has been discovered that, out of caution due to the complex and important nature of the case, the First Special Court has decided to form a joint panel to hear the case. The panel will be composed of Criminal Court President Qian Hongye and Judges Feng Shide and Xiao Xiefei. The hearing time has also been postponed to the afternoon. The hearing court may be changed to the First Criminal Court. The lawyer representing the Public Works Department in the prosecution has been designated as Ru Baoyi (the previous reports erroneously named Chiang Baolian). It is also said that the Procuratorate of the First Special Court will also appoint a prosecutor to appear in court to perform their duties. However, it is also necessary to continue to describe the process of arresting the perpetrators, so the record is being pursued.

After the murder occurred, the public security authorities of the Public Concession, and the Japanese military officers and police officers, recovered a PB-brand pistol about 90 yards from the scene of the incident, determining that it was the murder weapon used to shoot Nakayama Hideo. Based on this, an investigation was launched. A few days later, Deputy Inspector Nakamura Nagao of the Japanese Police Station received a report from Japanese detective Hairama Sugis that the murderers in the case were a Korean named Jack and two Chinese, one called "Little Guangdong," and one other unknown person. The pistol belonged to Jack. It was said that on the night of November 9th, Jack and "Little Guangdong" and two others, walking on Baole'an Road, happened to meet Nakayama. Near Fengle Village, Jack handed the pistol to "Little Guangdong," who then assassinated Nakayama. However, the three immediately fled after the incident, so their whereabouts were unknown. After receiving the news, Nakamura Nagao believed that the case had a lead and ordered Hairara to conduct further investigation. Soon, Nakamura received Hairala's second report, stating that it had been found that "Little Guangdong" was a member of the Triad society, familiar with a senior member of the society named Zeng Yuanchen. According to Zeng, in October of last year, "Little Guangdong" had pledged a pistol resembling a PB brand pistol to him, but he had refused due to lack of funds and returned the pistol. It was also learned that "Little Guangdong" had left Shanghai for Qingdao in November of last year, and then returned. In December of the same year, he took several dancing girls to Qingdao and opened the Vienna Dance Hall on Cangkou Road in Qingdao until February of this year, when he returned to Shanghai, went to the Yangzi Dance Hall for several days, and then left Shanghai for Qingdao again. After receiving this report, Nakamura Nagao instructed Haira to make a special appointment to meet with a member of the Triad, and put the PB brand pistol together with three other pistols for the Triad member to identify. The PB brand was pointed out, saying that it was what "Little Guangdong" had pledged to him. At this point, Nakamura believed that the leads were indeed close to the truth. On April 12th, he led several Japanese detectives and Zeng Yuanchen to Qingdao and went directly to the Vienna Dance Hall, where Zeng pointed out the appearance of "Little Guangdong". Zeng Yuanchen only knew that "Little Guangdong"'s surname was Ye, but did not know his name. After Nakamura Nagao returned to Shanghai, on April 14th, he requested the Legal Group of the Public Works Department to request a public letter from the First Special District Court to transfer the prisoner, stating that there was a murderer named Ye, nicknamed "Little Guangdong," who had been detained in Qingdao. Due to the request of the Legal Group of the Public Works Department, the court issued a public letter to transfer the prisoner on the same day. Nakamura Nagao, holding this public letter, led several Japanese detectives and flew to Qingdao on April 15th. The director of the Qingdao Municipal Public Security Bureau, after reviewing the public letter submitted by Nakamura Nagao, was deeply shocked because the bureau had not detained a prisoner named Ye, so how could there be a public letter to transfer him? Nakamura Nagao then stated to the bureau that the prisoner Ye had not been detained and requested assistance in the arrest. The director of the bureau believed that the procedure was not appropriate and that the public letter to transfer could not be used as an arrest warrant. Later, Nakamura Nagao used other procedures to finally arrest "Little Guangdong" and escort him to Shanghai. This is the process of "Little Guangdong" being arrested. This "Little Guangdong" is Ye Haisheng, about 28 or 29 years old. On April 19th, the Detewe Road Police Station requested the First Special District Court to issue two search warrants, one for No. 36 in a certain village on Oujia Road and one for a certain village on Tangshan Road, saying that wanted criminals were hiding at the above two locations. The court issued the search warrants on the same day. The Detewe Road Police Station sent several Japanese detectives to search Oujia Road first, but found nothing. Then they went to Tangshan Road to search. In a certain house number, they found an English physics book. The book was hardcover, with a hole dug inside, the size of which was similar to that of a BP brand pistol. One side of the book resembled an imprint of the characters BP. The owner of the house was named Yang Wendao, about 40 years old, from Guangdong. Yang was the president of the Shanghai Compatriots Association, which had a certificate of registration approved by the authorities. Therefore, Yang was arrested. Also arrested was Chen Rongsheng, a Cantonese man in his thirties, who was a member of the Compatriots Association because he had close dealings with Yang. This is the story of how Yang and Chen were arrested. Yang and Chen were sent to the First Special Court on the afternoon of April 20th to apply for detention. "Little Guangdong" Ye Haisheng applied for detention on April 21st. All are now held in special rooms in the Central Police Station.

During the investigation, Yang Wendao admitted that he had once possessed a BP brand pistol, but that the gun had been lost for more than a year. Yang also admitted that the English quantity study book belonged to him, but he firmly denied any knowledge of the Nakayama Hideo murder case. Chen Rongsheng absolutely denied any connection with the Nakayama Hideo case. "Little Guangdong" Ye Haisheng confessed that the reason he was poor in the past and now has money is that his wife, Chen Guizhen, is a dancer detained in the Public Security Bureau. After leaving the dance hall a few years ago, Guizhen entered the dance hall and met a wealthy merchant surnamed Wang. Last year, Wang died of illness and Guizhen inherited the estate. Guizhen reunited with him last year, so he now has the capital to open a dance hall, not from murder. He denied the murder. The police department now recognizes "Little Guangdong" Ye Haisheng as the prime culprit in the Nakayama Hideo case, Yang Wendao as the instigator, Chen Rongsheng as having a lesser relationship, and the Korean Jack as the principal offender, and believes that the case does not have political implications. It is said that Haisheng also confessed that although he knew the Korean Jack, he had fought with him because of a loan dispute. Ye and Yang Chen both denied knowing Zeng Yuanchen. According to those close to the Legal Group of the Public Works Department, the Legal Group analyzed the Yang Chen Ye suspects from a legal perspective, and the evidence of the crime was insufficient. The court considered the case to be serious and decided to hold a joint hearing on April 27th (i.e. today) at about 2:00 PM, presided over by Criminal Court President Qian Hongye and judges Feng Shide and Xiao Xiefei. According to news from the Fan Gang Law Office, the court designated lawyers such as Fan to provide pro bono defense for Ye Haisheng, Yang Wendao, and Chen Rongsheng. It is said that the hearing may not prohibit public attendance.

Jinlong Silk Weaving Factory: Lawsuit After Closure Awaits Investigation.

Qian Qizong and Jiang Linshu, currently managers of the Dalun Silk Fabric Bureau on Nanjing Road in Shanghai, and Jiang Changlin, who currently resides at No. 5, Lane 473, Aivin Yi Road, jointly established the Jinlong Silk Weaving Factory in 1931, with a total capital of 24,000 yuan. Jiang held half of the shares, and the rest was raised by Qian and others. After starting the business, unexpectedly, the losses were very large, and it was soon closed down. Jiang appointed accountant Wang Zikang to review the accounts and discovered many irregularities. Jiang had no choice but to hire lawyer Ge Zhaoji to file a complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing Qian Qizong, Jiang Linshu, Pan Shenchu, Qian Yaozhen, and four others of fraud, embezzlement, breach of trust, and other crimes. The other day was the date for the continuation of the trial. According to the plaintiff Jiang Changlin, he and Qian and others jointly formed the Jinlong Silk Weaving Factory in 1931, with an authorized capital of 24,000 yuan, agreed to be a limited liability company, appointed Qian Qizong as supervisor, Jiang Linshu as supervisor, in charge of money in and out, and Pan Shenchu as manager, specializing in factory scheduling. Who knew that after each person took office, until the business closed, they not only did not perform their duties, but also committed illegal acts. When Qian Yaozhen, the manager of the Yongfeng Silk Village, signed a contract with the Jinlong Silk Factory, he and Qian, Jiang, and others colluded in fraud, so he was also listed as a defendant. As for the facts of each person's crime, the first was erosion of capital. The capital of the Jinlong Silk Weaving Factory was calculated at 24,000 yuan, and the plaintiff recognized half of the shares, a total of six shares, totaling 12,000 yuan. However, the capital book only recorded the receipt of 6,000 yuan from the plaintiff. The report of accountant Pan Xulun also showed the same, a difference of half the amount. Qian and Jiang held important positions and were in charge of money in and out, but they did not record the plaintiff's remaining half of the shares in the register, and their responsibility for embezzlement was undeniable. The second was dereliction of duty and fraud. The Jinlong Factory's general ledger recorded the payment of 800 yuan in expenses to a certain bureau on May 24, 1934, 50 yuan to a certain bureau, and 20 yuan in clothing materials to a certain bureau. If the above three items were true, then Qian and Jiang committed bribery under Article 122, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law. If they were false, then it was an overpayment and close to pocketing the funds, violating Article 339, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law for fraud. In the middle, there was also a record of four payments of 2,800 yuan in remuneration to Qian Shaoji. It was absurd that the business was not doing well and the company was heavily in debt, so how could there be any remuneration? Moreover, there was no such person as Qian Shaoji among the staff, so it was known that they colluded to commit fraud. As for Pan Shenchu, there was suspicion of perjury, because Pan testified in the civil court of the First Special District that the Jinlong Factory's liquidation expenses at the time were six or seven thousand yuan, which Pan borrowed from the Yongfeng Silk Village, but this was a false statement intended to make the plaintiff bear an unrequired debt, so he was accused of perjury. Qian Yaozhen was the manager of the Yongfeng Silk Village and the brother of Qian Qizong. The actual number of products in stock at the Jinlong Factory was more than 25,000 yuan. According to the contract with Yongfeng, the mortgage ratio was limited to 70%, so Yongfeng only needed to advance more than 17,000 yuan. Now, Qian Yaozhen of the Yongfeng Silk Village has advanced funds exceeding the fixed amount, reaching 35,000 yuan, which not only violated the contract but was actually colluding with his brothers Qian Qizong and Jiang Linshu to commit fraud. Furthermore, the contract stated that the Yongfeng Silk Village should collect and remit the funds for the goods sold by the Jinlong Factory at any time. However, in 1933, the Yongfeng sold Jinlong goods worth more than 178,000 yuan, which should have been transferred at any time, but the village delayed the transfer until February 1934, causing the Jinlong to lose more than 12,000 yuan in interest. Thus, Qian Yaozhen of the Yongfeng Village fraudulently obtained illegal interest and betrayed others, violating the crime of fraud and breach of trust under the Criminal Law and attaching a private prosecution, seeking compensation for losses totaling 63,700 yuan. Subsequently, the defendant Qian Qizong replied that the reason for the underreporting of the capital at the time was to avoid the attention of the workers, so it was recorded in the books at half the amount, with no intention of embezzlement. As for the payment to a certain bureau, it was handled by another person and was of a nature similar to remuneration. As for the reason for the total transfer of business income, it was because the entire year's business was not in cash until the end of the year, when it was collected, so it was transferred once at the end of the final settlement. As for the remuneration to Qian Shaoji, it was all with the consent of the plaintiff. Then, the plaintiff questioned the defendant in court, asking whether the remuneration was cash or gifts. The defendant replied that it was a gift certificate. When asked which store's gift certificate, he replied that it was the Bank of China or the Shanghai Bank, but he could not remember. Later, accountant Wang Zikang confirmed to the court the discrepancies in the Jinlong Factory's various account books. The court then adjourned the case to 2:00 PM on the 29th for further questioning due to the need to summon witnesses and conduct investigations.

A Suicide Note Exhausts a Lifetime of Pain. Min Shanbao's Suicide by Drowning is Pitiable. Yang Shenzhi's Abandonment Cannot Escape the Law. - A Letter to the Fellow Workers' Auxiliary Yuantang Requesting Public Announcement -

The other day, the Fellow Workers' Auxiliary Yuantang branch on Ningbo Road in the French Concession received a strange letter delivered by mail. The original letter is transcribed below:

Uncle Jingru, My pitiful self, unfortunately, my father passed away from illness when I was only three years old. My mother and I were left alone and helpless. Later, I was pitied by an elder, who gave us a monthly living allowance of 12 yuan, which was enough to keep us warm and fed. In 1925, my cousin, Yang Shenzhi, who worked at the Zhengda Xiang store at Dadongmen, saw that my mother was living alone and pretended to be solicitous. Soon, he seduced her and they began living together in a rented house in Juxin Village, Nanshi. At that time, I was still unaware of such matters. In 1926, Shenzhi resigned for some reason. Later, through the introduction of his sister, he became an employee of the Guanshengyuan General Company, and is now responsible for collecting accounts for the company. In 1927, Shenzhi returned to his hometown to get married. In the winter of that year, my mother gave birth to a son, named Quansheng, who is now nine years old. Shenzhi loves him as the apple of his eye. At that time, I was slightly aware of such matters, and entered primary school for two years. Later, I transferred to the Ai Qun Girls' School.

Time flies, and years pass quickly. Then, the Shanghai War broke out, and the elder's living allowance suddenly stopped, leaving me unable to continue my studies. I dropped out of school and returned home to help my mother with household chores. Who knew that the 128 Disaster Star arrived? In the winter of that year, Shenzhi saw that I was becoming more attractive and my affections were beginning to blossom. He gradually began to harbor inappropriate thoughts, and often

Economic Supplement: Finance in Extraordinary Times by Zhang Yifan

Taxes? Public Debt?

During the European War, the policy issues regarding how various countries raised funds for war expenses sparked widespread debate. The unfolding war situation, the ever-increasing demand for war funds, and the urgency of time constraints deeply concerned the financial authorities of various countries. The expenditures for years of war preparation, the detrimental effects of capital accumulation, and ordinary financial problems were already pressing matters, let alone the extraordinary times and the extraordinary demands they brought!

In ancient and medieval times, war expenses were mostly paid from accumulated reserves in peacetime, supplemented by tax levies and requisitions. Victors could also use spoils of war and reparations to make up for the expenses. Later, with the development of public credit, especially after the mid-eighteenth century, public debt gradually replaced the position of accumulated reserves. At this time, the purpose of taxation was only to provide funds for paying debt interest or as a debt repayment fund.

However, while the issuance of public debt can quickly raise a significant amount of revenue, it inherently has the disadvantage of inflating credit. Moreover, purchasing public debt is equivalent to investment. Marx said that this is a method for the bourgeoisie to accumulate capital, which is indeed a profound insight. Therefore, if wartime finance relies on public debt, on one hand, a vast number of hard-working people are shedding blood on the front lines, sacrificing themselves for the country, or tightening their belts in the rear, working diligently. On the other hand, a small number of bourgeois individuals are sitting back and enjoying huge profits in the rear, taking the opportunity to get rich. Once the war ends, ordinary people may have no choice but to pay heavy taxes to repay the national debt. This phenomenon is most likely to arouse dissatisfaction and create a trend of social unrest. Therefore, the bourgeoisie also feels that the issue is serious and cannot be treated casually. Thus, whether war expenses should be covered by public debt or by taxation has become the center of controversy.

Seligman, Plehn, and others advocated that wartime expenditures should be solely financed by public debt. This is because public debt places the burden on the future, while also reducing the direct pain of increased taxes for the people during wartime. It can also avoid the adverse effects of tax pressure on wartime industry and commerce, enabling them to continuously supply the resources needed for the war. Moreover, the governments of Germany and France believed that public debt was not the ultimate burden on the people and could easily be recovered from the enemy in the future. Therefore, the means of raising war funds almost entirely relied on public debt. The war debt raised by Germany accounted for a staggering 104.4% of the total war expenses. The proportion of war debt raised by France also reached 100.3% of the total war expenses. This situation not only indicates that their entire war expenses were reliant on public debt, but also indicates that some other expenses were also paid for by public debt. However, as a result, Germany was defeated and not only failed to recover from the enemy, but also had to be extorted for huge reparations. The national credit completely collapsed. France, on the other hand, forcibly demanded reparations, not hesitating to use force as a backing. Therefore, although the war has ended, the disputes still exist, and military expenditures continue to increase. Domestically, there is also a public opinion that demands reparations and opposes taxes, plunging public finances into extreme chaos.

Pigou of the United Kingdom, Sprague and Durant of the United States, and others believed that war expenses should be met with taxation. This is because taxation can prevent credit inflation from disrupting the social economy, avoid unequal distribution of the burden of war expenses, and avoid disrupting the financial system. This view is originally of great value. However, the essential requirements of wartime finance are rapid revenue and a large amount of funds. Taxation is relatively difficult. Therefore, looking at the results of tax revenue in various countries during the European War, the ratio to war expenses is generally very low. The tax revenue performance of the United Kingdom was better, but in the first year of the war, it was only 7%. Although it increased later, the overall average was still only 20%. On the other hand, those reliant on public debt accounted for 75.3%. Although the tax revenue performance of the United States was even better, at 31.7%, the ratio of national debt to the general total war expenses still accounted for 80.6%. As for other countries, the taxes levied by France during the war were not even enough to cover ordinary recurring expenses in peacetime; the new tax revenues of Italy were only sufficient to pay the interest on war debts. Germany could not even pay the interest, and the situation was similar in other countries.

Some people argue that war expenses should be entirely maintained by taxation, so as not to disrupt finance and avoid credit inflation. However, during the transitional period before new taxes become abundant, temporary borrowing can be used to cope with the situation. This method is generally recognized by the public in principle and is also adopted by the authorities of various countries in practice. However, as the war prolonged, the borrowing policy had to continue to be used. As a result, the desire to have limited inflation was still practically impossible to achieve. As can be seen from the active adoption of tax policies by the United Kingdom and the United States during the European War.

There were also a few British people who advocated establishing a type of permanent tax (Limpot Dermant) to maintain all public expenditures during and after the war. This stems from the argument for a military tax system and is a policy adorned with militaristic ideology. However, given the existence of the capital accumulation process in capitalist society, there is no hope that any tax can have such broad flexibility.

At the beginning of the United States' participation in the war, Treasury Secretary McAdoo advocated that war expenses should be equally distributed between taxes and public debt. In other words, half of the war expenses should be covered by tax revenue, and half by public debt revenue.

However, it is practically impossible to maintain this balanced limit. The reason is the same as the impossibility of the third proposition. Therefore, in the McAdoo era, in the 1917 fiscal year, expenses paid by tax revenue accounted for about 55%, but by 1918—the year after entering the war—the proportion of tax revenue had slowed down to 31.6%.

Before the end of the war, some people in France argued that all recurring expenses should be covered by tax revenue, while military expenses and pensions should be covered by public debt.

This budgetary division is not a good policy in terms of the financial system; moreover, is its actual effect not just increasing taxes on one hand and borrowing on the other?

Originally, these issues vary depending on the environment and actual situation of each country. For example, France was invaded by the enemy after the war broke out, and although the invaded area was not large, it was an economically important region. Therefore, its tax base naturally caused panic. At the same time, there was a considerable number of rentier classes in its social strata. Therefore, the complete reliance on public debt could represent the forces behind their government. As for Germany, it was originally the most rampant militaristic country. It held a determined belief in victory in the last war. Therefore, raising public debt was akin to giving the people a guaranteed investment. As for the United States, it had already invested a lot in war bonds to the Allied countries, so it wanted to extract its domestic financial burden from the general public. This precisely demonstrates the true nature of a rising capitalist country. As for the United Kingdom, because its tax system was more sound than other countries, its society's taxable capacity also had great flexibility. The proposition of relying on taxation was not a mere fantasy.

Domestic View Exploration

Now, we are also forced to study these issues. However, putting aside all vested interests, speaking only from the perspective of practical ability: then, wanting to increase taxes, the usual donations and taxes have already overwhelmed the people; issuing public debt, the society's surplus funds, even if pouring out all its possessions, it is unknown how many days of war expenses can be maintained? Because, our people's income is much lower than others; our society's surplus funds are much less than others; our tax system is unsound; and our credit institutions are not modernized. All this demonstrates that our country's wartime resources are extremely empty; our country's financial elasticity is pitifully weak. Even the peacetime financial budget is still precarious and mortgaging the future; let alone encountering this extraordinary demand. Therefore, although there are many opinions expressed by both the government and the public regarding this issue, everyone does not have a proper solution. Therefore, everyone's attitude is almost uniformly holding to "[regardless of the type of financial resources, as long as there is some revenue: regardless of the amount, regardless of the interests, only taking is the goal]." For example:

Ma Yinchu and others advocated using income tax as the main source of revenue, and if necessary, implementing a limited paper currency policy, and issuing a small amount of public debt to supplement it.

Zhu Guangze and others have the same opinion.

Income tax is indeed one of the best tax systems. But the problem is that the income of most people is minimal, how much can be available for national use? Since the main revenue does not have much hope, wanting to implement a limited paper currency policy, the result is only unlimited expansion. Wanting to issue a limited amount of public debt, the result can only be unlimited issuance. Therefore, although the theory is extremely in line with financial principles, the effect has no choice but to go down a path against one's will. In the future, it will only have to rely on dangerous paper currency policies and public debt policies from beginning to end. The so-called "income tax as the main source of revenue" is "drawing a cake to satisfy hunger," as Xiao Shuyu said, which is not an exaggeration.

War expenses should be maintained simultaneously by increased taxes and borrowing. And bonds should be both domestic and foreign. As for paper currency policies, they are absolutely opposed. This is the proposition of Wei Tingsheng and others.

There is also someone who almost entirely copied Wei's book "Wartime Finance" in the Economic Quarterly and echoed it.

However, if increased taxes and borrowing do not have other prerequisites and appropriate preparations, as a result, on the one hand, there will be heavy and tyrannical levies, the people cannot bear it; and the revenue is still insignificant; on the other hand, credit inflation still forms a world of paper currency overflow. The lessons learned by various countries during the European War are.

Zhu Xi believed that the way out for China's wartime finance should start from those with the ability to bear the burden, but who have no direct burden on the country. His goal is to implement: municipal land value tax, land appreciation tax; and bank income tax. However, this income is extremely limited, and Zhu is well aware of it. Therefore, he also proposed ten fundamental measures: preparing war special profit tax, preparing entertainment tax, increasing the tax rate on luxury goods, increasing stamp duty, increasing postage, allocating according to property, implementing saving the country donation, free donation, borrowing foreign debt, implementing paper currency policies when necessary, and reducing unnecessary expenditures. Two Two, however, the tax revenue part is all small in income and will greatly disturb the people. The part on soliciting donations is either not easy to handle and has little effect (free donation), or has a great effect but is difficult to handle (saving the country donation). As for raising foreign debt, where the creditor is is the first problem; paper currency policies are extremely dangerous.

I believe that wartime tax policies should also adhere to the principles of "avoiding harshness and detail" and "minimum sacrifice." Public debt and paper currency are both extremely dangerous policies, but even countries as wealthy and strong as European and American countries cannot avoid them, let alone our country. However, how to reduce the danger, how to make it safe and fair, is the main issue. In short, the attitude we must adhere to in raising war funds is: "How to quickly concentrate a large amount of funds within the possible scope and safe limits to meet the needs of the war; and also have the ability to sustain it for a long time. All that is sought is quick results, using any means, this is not a solution after all. If one drinks poison to quench thirst and acts rashly, then the danger may be the same as war. Because to ensure victory in the war, one must have manpower (Mau), material resources (Munton), and financial resources (Money), and none of them can be lacking.

Wartime financial policy, if it can obtain a large amount of revenue, has already fulfilled its responsibility to the war. But if it incites social unrest due to unscrupulous means, losing the conditions of "unity against foreign enemies" and "determination to fight" in "manpower," the result will be that even if it is not defeated by the war, it will be defeated by finance. "What defeated Germany was not the war, but the revolutionary sentiment in the army." The financial authorities should pay close attention to this famous saying.

What the war machine truly needs is not currency, but material resources. Material resources can be continuously supplied for war use only under continuous and smooth production. War has already given production great resistance. If finance puts another pressure on it, this is a self-destructive approach. Tax policies and public debt policies are both like double-edged swords to production. On the one hand, they can help it remove thorns, and on the other hand, they can take its life. It all depends on how they are used.

Currency is only an intermediary for making war obtain the necessary material resources; it is not the main purpose of wartime finance. As long as credit institutions are sound and the means of implementation are appropriate, it can be solved. Therefore, our economic capacity does not allow us to choose wartime financial resources as scholars in the United Kingdom and the United States do, should war expenses be paid by taxes? Or should war expenses be paid by public debt? And so on this simple question. Because of our scarce resources, absorbing from multiple sources is good, and it is also necessary. What we are concerned about is what methods can be used to avoid various potential dangers and be within "safe limits." However, the general public always regards paper currency policies as a last resort. Therefore, this article will temporarily leave this issue aside and focus on discussing what policies we should adopt for taxation and public debt during wartime.

Wartime Tax Policies

Now, let's first discuss wartime tax policies.

There are four significant advantages to implementing tax policies during wartime:

In terms of prices: Although indirect taxes can raise prices due to transfer, their power is less than that of credit inflation. (However, avoiding them is the best policy) Direct taxes are mostly non-transferable, so they have no impact on prices. Prices do not skyrocket (during wartime, price increases are always unavoidable due to increased demand and unavoidable credit inflation). On the one hand, people's hearts are more stable, and livelihoods are easier; on the other hand, wartime industries can also proceed smoothly.

In terms of material resources: Reducing consumption for war use is one of the real resources during wartime.

Increasing taxes results in the invisible restriction of people's consumption. Beneficial to the war.

In terms of finance: Public debt is actually future taxes; and in order to show national credit, when borrowing, new taxes are set up or tax rates are increased as funds for repayment of principal and interest. Therefore, in finance, it is just drinking poison to quench thirst, increasing the burden. Taxes unconditionally seize a portion of the national income. Therefore, the government does not increase the burden; for the people, it is actually equivalent to reducing the burden of public debt interest.

In terms of society: Debt is easy to arouse social injustice; the burden of the tax system, as long as it conforms to the principle of equal sacrifice, can gain the support of the majority of the people; even those who have resentment are only a small portion of the bourgeoisie. Therefore, it is not enough to affect the overall situation.

However, taxes also have two major shortcomings:

Raising taxes is slow to take effect, which is not in line with the urgent needs of wartime.

The burden of taxes is added to the present. Therefore, it is a restriction on national income: revenue is difficult to be abundant. If the tax system is poor, it is especially easy to arouse social unrest, and reduce the social economic production capacity.

This is from the perspective of tax theory. As for based on our country's actual situation, there are more reasons why tax policy is not enough to solve the entire war expense problem. The main ones are:

The places with greater national income, that is, places with more tax revenue, must be cities with developed production industries. Our country's largest cities, such as Shanghai, Tianjin, Jinan, Qingdao, Wuxi, Hankou, Guangzhou, Shantou, Xiamen, Ningbo, Hangzhou, etc., are either along the coast or along the river, and some have already fallen under the enemy's power, and some are also places that the enemy is preparing to seize. Therefore, once the war occurs, the above-mentioned places all have the possibility of being successively occupied by the enemy. Therefore, the existing three major sources of salt, tariffs, and customs are no longer ours; let alone being able to dig up other new tax sources.

Our country's production is backward, and national income is extremely low. As far as the current situation is concerned, in addition to paying taxes, livelihoods have become a problem.

The impact of social and economic panic in recent years, all industries have declined; especially the rural economy is even more miserable.

Tax resources are distributed throughout the country: In our country with a corrupt and unbearable collection system, even in peacetime, it is not possible to achieve public good with every bit of revenue. If there is no strict supervision, the wartime situation will be even more unbearable.

Economic separatism formed by political separatism is currently rampant in provinces with expanding feudal forces. Therefore, interception and tax withholding have not yet disappeared. Although this is a political issue and has to be put aside, it cannot be excluded from our considerations.

Therefore, our wartime tax policy, in addition to political issues that need to be resolved with political methods, from a financial standpoint: one party should do its best to give play to its advantages: under this purpose, we must first cultivate the foundation of national resources. What the war needs is material resources, and what the people need is "income." The only means to obtain this effect is to increase production. Therefore, Pigou believes that increasing production is one of the main resources during wartime.

In our country, where production is backward and declining, in this extraordinary period, we must implement national defense economic construction. The source of construction funds should come from expanding credit.

Because its production has a price, it should be obtained from public debt with investment properties. It can avoid the burden of increased taxes on the general public in addition to being oppressed by profits. At the same time, this type of credit inflation has no drawbacks. The prices raised by inflation are still suppressed by increased production.

On the other hand: we should try our best to avoid its shortcomings. Under this purpose, we should earnestly base ourselves on the principles of "minimum sacrifice" and "equal sacrifice." These two principles are not mutually opposed. The former is to make the people bear the amount of the "minimum sacrifice"; the latter is to make the distribution of the people's burden conform to the substantial "equality of sacrifice." Therefore, this "equality" is not an equal division of the burden, nor is it a proportional burden, but a progressive grant to various classes with substantial equality in sacrifice, so that the tax system can play the role of adjusting distribution in order to avoid its shortcomings as much as possible.

Based on the above-mentioned principles and special circumstances, we propose the following for tax policies and related policies:

Implement a progressive income tax, inheritance tax, wealth tax, and excess profits tax (including land appreciation tax, wartime excess profits tax, excessive profits, etc.) that are more emphasized than in peacetime. As for luxury tax and entertainment tax, they have long lost their qualification as my source under wartime consumption control; therefore, there is no need to increase the tax rate further, but given our country's special circumstances, there may be a possibility of appropriately increasing them.

Improve the collection system, strictly supervise management; both physical objects and currency should be used for collection methods. For example, agricultural tax, sales tax related to war use, sales tax related to monopoly, etc., can all adopt the physical object collection system, while income tax, inheritance tax, wealth tax, excess profits tax, etc., can still use the currency collection system depending on the circumstances.

The main advantages of adopting the physical object collection system are four: (A) the income can be directly used for war use and public sales, (B) it can help the implementation of wartime price control policies, (C) it can reduce the opportunity for tax officials to embezzle and make personal gains, because it is more difficult to embezzle physical objects than to embezzle currency. (D) it can avoid producers from being oppressed and exploited by commercial capital. However, there is also one shortcoming: (A) collection fees may increase, (B) storage and collection procedures are more complicated, (C) transportation is time-consuming, but these shortcomings are not difficult to prevent: (A) implement physical object exchange, (B) nationalize transportation, (C) implement price control, (D) establish state-managed commercial centers. Detailed methods will be discussed in a special article.

Appropriately adopt the tax farming system. In order to cope with the urgent expenditures during wartime, the tax farming system can be adopted for taxes with slow collection. However, its drawbacks can easily lead to tax farmers using their power to harass the people. Therefore, it may be better to organize a tax company run by merchants and supervised by officials. In addition to contracting tax collection, it can also underwrite treasury bills. The establishment of the tax farming system can reduce the tax collection expenses. The amount of this reduction can be used as the maximum limit for contracting profits, which seems more appropriate.

Register luxury goods such as gold, silver, jewelry, ornaments, works of art, antiques, etc. Implement requisition, confiscation, or purchase when necessary. This income is used as a part of offsetting the price of international lending. I firmly believe that if it can be handled properly, the amount of income will be considerable. However, it only has practical value before the external transportation and communication in Shanghai are cut off, and this disturbance will inevitably be unbearable.

Implement a large-scale public sales policy to offset the losses of salt tax, consolidated tax, and customs duties affected by the war. Such as table salt, kerosene, coal, matches, tea, silk, sugar, tung oil, tobacco, alcohol, and even cotton, wheat, etc. Except for the four types of table salt, tobacco, alcohol, and matches, others are all those that have significant relationships with international trade. Therefore, they should also be uniformly listed as commodities for public sale. As for the production and consumption of tobacco and alcohol, they should be vigorously banned or restricted during wartime. In order to divert this consumer capital for wartime resources. Therefore, it has already lost its value for public sale. However, it should still be listed as a commodity for public sale.

In order to facilitate the implementation of the above-mentioned plans and to adapt to the extraordinary state of the wartime economy, a wartime economic control policy should be implemented immediately and engage in national defense economic construction. These funds are raised by expanding government credit.

Because of the effect of economic construction, material production can be increased, national income can be improved, and society will enter prosperity, and wartime resources can be inexhaustible. Thus, on the one hand, most of the material resources needed for the war can be self-sufficient; and the ability to resist economic blockade can be slightly increased. On the other hand: the public expenditures, of which those that are consumptive (such as those transferred to foreigners due to contractual relationships) can be gradually reduced; and those that are transferable (those transferred to domestic people due to contractual or obligation relationships) can be increased day by day; so that social resources can flow in a smooth state.

In addition, forced donations and requisitions can also be done occasionally; however, postal surcharges, stamp duty rate increases, and business tax rate increases, etc., should be avoided as appropriate. One reason is that the income is not large, the second reason is that it can be transferred, and the third reason is that it forms a multiple tax with the above-mentioned newly levied and heavily levied taxes. They will all severely harm people's livelihood. When creating new taxes or adding new tax rates, we should vigorously strike at the production of wartime industries. Otherwise, it will be a loss outweighing the gain.

Wartime Public Debt Policy

Next, we can discuss our wartime public debt policy.

The raising of war expenses takes "rapid" and "huge amount" as two major requirements. Countries that do not have war preparation savings have no other way to cope with emergency expenditures during wartime other than public debt. Countries with strong taxable capacity still cannot rely entirely on taxation for war expenses in the future. Not to mention those with weak taxable capacity. Therefore, this is a matter of fact; what is worth discussing is only how to make it safe.

As mentioned earlier, public debt policy contains great dangers. The main ones are: First, it forms credit inflation, resulting in inflation. Second, it increases the financial burden, making finance a private distribution administration for creditors; third, it increases the inappropriate burden on the principal and interest of public debt for the people; fourth, it increases the process of capital concentration and accumulation, and emphasizes inequality in social distribution; fifth, it violates the principle of "equal sacrifice" in finance.

However: on the one hand, there is an inevitable trend to issue public debt for compensation; on the other hand, there is a contradiction of causing social and economic unrest; we cannot stop eating because we are afraid of choking, and we cannot drink poison to quench our thirst; the only way is to seek a way out within a relatively safe limit.

Regarding the "safe limit" of public debt policy, I believe that the following four major conditions must be met:

First, the issuance of credit has the ability to automatically regulate; it will not disrupt finance and affect prices. For example, if the funds for public enterprise come from credit, there is this possibility of automatic regulation. Such as foreign debt, although it has no regulatory power, it also has no destructive power.

Second, slow down the process of capital accumulation and concentration. This is important, but it is impossible to turn the social system upside down. Therefore, at present, we can only say "slow down." I believe that during wartime, one should not adopt high interest rates, tax exemptions, etc. to induce the sale of public debt. This is not only harmful to finance itself, but also not really necessary, because during wartime, it is safer for people to purchase and store public debt than to store currency. An appropriate publicity campaign can also arouse the people's patriotism to help the issuance of public debt. Tax exemption for public debt is truly an enemy of the wealth tax system. It is not allowed at any time. In addition, I believe that in the period of financial consolidation after the war, in order to reduce the financial burden, a special debt redemption levy should be created. According to the people's ability to pay taxes, it should be levied on individual net worth (referring to capital rather than income) on a progressive basis with a certain tax-exempt limit. The payment period should be short, and the means of payment can allow the use of public debt securities. The creation of this special donation was advocated by many people in the United Kingdom after the war. Dalton even thought that it was "at least representative of those sitting at home, paying back a moral debt to those who were running around on the battlefield and losing economic opportunities."

Third, try to prevent the connection between government credit and bank credit. For example, in our country today, various public debt regulations stipulate that public debt tickets can be used as guarantee reserves for bank issuance of paper money. Therefore, the result of the expansion of government credit is the creation of bank paper money expansion. If we want to make wartime government credit also have a considerable possibility of expansion in order to meet the needs of unavoidable wartime, then we need to first change the public debt regulations, at least cancel the legal qualification that wartime public debt can also be used as a guarantee reserve, in order to sever the connection between government credit and bank credit; only in this way can such government credit, after a considerable expansion, still be obtained within the safe limit.

Fourth, try to prevent government credit from exceeding the saturation capacity of social digestion of public debt, because the result is that either the public debt reserve immediately shakes; or after inflation, the currency credit, and even the entire financial institution, go bankrupt at the same time, because the public debt exceeds the social digestion capacity. The central bank will lose its commanding power to maintain the price of the debt market (that is, credit). Regardless of whether the bondholder is for speculative purposes or for the purpose of exchanging for a certain capital, they spit out a huge amount of public debt on the market, but the market is unable to digest it, resulting in a price drop. The central bank is unable to maintain it, which means that the government is unable to maintain credit. If credit shakes and they rush to sell, this trend will become unstoppable. If the central bank increases the issuance of paper money in order to maintain the debt market, the result is that the monetary system is sacrificed, but the public debt still comes to the same end. Especially during wartime, government credit is most easily shaken; the market atmosphere is also most easily confused. Therefore, the crisis of the storm is always there. The government's credit can determine the victory or defeat of the war; therefore, it must not be risked. If our wartime public debt policy operates within such a safe limit, then no matter what method it is issued, there will be no further objection.

However, when it comes to the method of issuance, I would like to propose two types of special public debt for everyone to study. I believe that it is most appropriate to advocate them during wartime.

Adopting the method of folk champion associations, issue a special type of public debt with the goal of promoting people's reduced consumption, borrowing of saved income, and diverting it to war use. Therefore, it can be named Savings Public Debt. Giving a slight interest rate and stipulating a fairly long term; for the people, it is equivalent to savings: therefore, it can also be called Wartime Savings Public Debt. However, this type of public debt is not freely raised, but is allocated according to each person's wealth; therefore, it is also different from the United Kingdom's wartime savings bonds and the savings bonds adopted by various countries. And it cannot be sold on the market, and it is cleared in one lump sum when it expires. The advantages of this method: there is the possibility of obtaining a considerable amount of revenue as a forced donation, without the deep pain that people feel when their income is taken away as a forced donation. It has the effectiveness of general public debt, but it does not have the shortcomings of general public debt; because it cannot be sold on the market, and the interest rate is low, so it does not cause the danger of a credit storm, nor does it excessively increase the financial burden. In nature, it is similar to income tax, but income tax is not returned after payment: but this one can still be recovered: therefore, it is easier to issue than to collect income tax.

Adopting the method of company gift certificates, issue a commodity substitute bond to borrow surplus or saved products from the people for war use: those that cannot be used for war can be handed over to state-run commercial centers for sale. This type of bond can enable both those who own inventory and general producers to purchase them, while also directly meeting the war's demand for material resources. This bond is still paid with goods upon repayment. After a certain period of time, the bondholder can freely exchange the goods they need from the state-run commercial center once or several times; after the price of the goods they take has reached the face value, it will be cleared. In order to facilitate sales, a slight interest rate is also given. This bond can be sold on the market. Because it is itself a personification of purchasing power, it is not enough to cause a general credit crisis.

Grain Market: Steady Early Rice, Weak Later Rice

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources of various gangs arrived, totaling more than thirty numbers, with a total of more than 6,000 piculs of goods. Both retail and wholesale were calm. The Tianjin gang only handled 1,000-odd packages in wholesale, so the market conditions were generally weak. Thick early rice continued to decline by several cents to one dime, thin rice slightly decreased, Doyang pointed rice fell by about a dime, the price remained flat and weak.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, the gangs from the lower reaches of the river arrived with twenty-two or three boats. The retail of white rice was unusually deserted, and the market price dropped by about one dime. Early rice was stable, the retail of thin rice was ordinary, the wholesale was slightly active, the market shape rose nearly one dime, the middle and secondary grades were stable, and various sen rice also showed a weak trend. Yin goods were scarce, and the price was stable. The retail of white rice was sluggish, and the price decreased by about one dime. The prices of other goods were weak.

Seafood: New Inkfish Will Soon Be on the Market

Inkfish is dried cuttlefish, commonly known as bird thief. It is produced in various coastal areas of Zhejiang, with Yangshan, Shengshan, Daishan, and Zhoushan having the most, followed by Sijiao, Huanglong, Liuheng, Huaniao, Chuanshan, Qushan, Shenjiamen, Ligang, and Wenzhou. There is also production in Yantai and the Jiangbei area, called North Inkfish, but the output is far less than Ningbo. However, the quality is extremely good, the muscles are thick and the size is large, and it is clean and beautiful, which cannot be compared with Ningbo products. The wholesale price is also always more than one package higher. Twenty years ago, there were also goods from Japan, with the same shape as North Inkfish. Later, due to the increasing domestic production and the cheaper price, they were rejected. Every early summer, fishing households go out to sea to catch them in partnership. If they encounter a bumper harvest, they can harvest more than 100,000 dan a year. If the ocean does not produce, there are also 60,000 to 70,000 dan. There are about 10,000 people who make a living from this. The sales market is very wide, such as Min, Guang, Chuan, Xiang, and Gan, all have huge needs. Currently, new goods have not yet appeared on the market, and the amount of old goods in stock is scarce. In the hands of the dealers, the statistics are less than 1,000 pieces, so the market situation is very stable. The wholesale price of large pieces of North Inkfish is 58 yuan, medium pieces are 55 yuan, Ningbo goods are 28 yuan for large pieces, 23-24 yuan for Gaozhuang, and 21-22 yuan for ordinary goods. The future market must look at the richness of the new year's harvest to determine the honor and disgrace.
